<<HEADING level=2>>National Foreword<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This British Standard is the UK implementation of BS EN 1090-2:2008.
It supersedes DD ENV 1090-1:1998  DD ENV 1090-4:2001,
DD ENV 1090-6:2001 which are withdrawn, and BS 5400- 6:1999,
BS 5950-2:2001 which will be withdrawn on March 2010.
The UK participation in its preparation was entrusted to Technical
Committee B/521 Execution of steel structures, with the assistance of
B/525/10 Bridges.
A list of organizations represented on this committee can be obtained on
request to its secretary.
Additional information
BSI, as a member of CEN, is obliged to publish EN 1090-2:2008 as a
British Standard. However, attention is drawn to the fact that during
the development of this European Standard, the UK committee voted
against its approval as a European Standard.
The reason for the UK committee vote was because of concerns about
possible misspecification in terms of execution classes and weld quality
levels in particular. If realized, these concerns about the range and the
basis of some of the choices could lead either to under-specification and
inadequate safety or to over-specification and possible barriers to trade.
These issues are described more fully below, together with suggestions
that should avoid these risks.
This standard gives the technical requirements for the execution
(fabrication and erection) of steel structures and is a supporting
standard for the harmonized standard BS EN 1090-1,  Execution of steel
structures and aluminium structures – Part 1: Requirements for
conformity assessment of structural components . Conformity assessment
to BS EN 1090-1 requires that the manufacturer operates a certified
factory production control system. The quality management
requirements for factory production control include, for instance, levels
of traceability and welding quality management which are defined by
reference to BS EN 1090-2.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>,<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This standard supersedes several existing standards and hence has a very wide scope.
Therefore, it requires specifiers to make a series of project- or application-specific
decisions before execution commences on each part of the works. Annex A itemizes the
additional and optional information required.
Execution classes
This standard introduces the concept of execution class (EXC) as a classified set of
requirements specified for the execution of the works as a whole, of an individual
component, or of a detail of a component. Annex A.3 itemizes those requirements in the
standard which depend on the choice of execution class.
It is a design decision for the specifier to select the execution class required for the works
as a whole, an individual component, or a particular detail of a component. Annex B of
BS EN 1090-2 provides some informative guidance on the factors that might be relevant
to that decision. The primary reason to differentiate is to provide a level of reliability
against failure or malfunction of the structure/component/detail that is matched to the
consequences (see BS EN 1990,  Eurocode – Basis of structural design , for further
information). Hence, execution class is widely used in this standard as a reliability
differentiator for providing choice of quality, testing and qualification requirements,
although the relationship between this new differentiator and those recommended by BS
EN 1990 is not fully defined.
Annex B of BS EN 1090-2 recommends that the choice of execution class should also
depend on the ‘service category’ (SC) that characterizes a component in terms of the
circumstances of its designed use, and the ‘production category’ (PC) that characterizes a
component in terms of the methods used for its execution. These latter two types of
category imply that, for a given structure/component/detail, the execution class specified
should be increased in line with more onerous demands in service and/or if it is more
difficult to produce.
From Annex B it appears likely that most steel structures in the UK will include
components in both PC1 and PC2, but most will be SC1 unless they are designed for
fatigue actions (in which case they will be SC2). Thus, as a default basis, EXC2 could be
specified for structures/components/details used in buildings, and EXC3 could be
specified for structures/components/details used in bridges.
Weld quality levels
For structures/components/details designed for fatigue additional requirements should
be adopted because the simple choice between design for quasi-static (SC1) and fatigue
(SC2) applications does not sufficiently discriminate the required weld quality levels in
terms of fatigue classes.
In these circumstances, as the choice of appropriate requirements requires a level of
design and construction knowledge that many potential users of this standard may not
possess, reference should be made to the advice given in PD 6695-1-9,  Recommendations
for the design of structures to BS EN 1993-1-9 , which explains the relationship between
design and execution with respect to fatigue classes (FAT classes), and PD 6705-2,
Recommendations for the execution of steel bridges to BS EN 1090-2 , which gives
acceptance criteria for welds designed for fatigue. These acceptance criteria have been
developed for structural welds on a fitness-for-purpose basis and are consistent with
those used in the British Standards that are superseded by BS EN 1090-2.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_4>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2 relates the execution classes to weld quality levels in BS EN ISO 5817,
Welding – Fusion-welded joints in steel, nickel, titanium and their alloys (beam welding
excluded) – Quality levels for imperfections , as follows:
•
EXC1: Quality level D;
•
EXC2: Quality level C generally;
•
EXC3: Quality level B (i.e. as required for welder qualification tests and welding
procedure qualification records);
•
EXC4: Quality level B+.
These levels may generally be appropriate to establish, prequalify and certificate the
routine quality level of the manufacturer’s welding operations. However, although EXC4
can be used to specify the extent of supplementary non-destructive testing, the
associated quality level B+ is not practically achievable in routine production as it
requires the manufacturer to demonstrate a capability of meeting a quality level which
is more stringent than that for which the manufacturer’s welders and welding
procedures are qualified. Thus, if a quality level of B or higher is required, it is more
practical to specify this for each relevant joint detail and not for routine production,
using the acceptance criteria given in PD 6705-2 for evaluating imperfections on an
individual basis, as permitted by BS EN 1090-2.
Tolerances
BS EN 1090-2 is more complicated than the British Standards that it supersedes in its
approach to specifying permitted geometrical deviations as systems of tolerances. Three
types of geometrical tolerance are defined:
1.
essential tolerances that are essential for the mechanical resistance and stability
of the completed structure and which are used to support conformity assessment
to BS EN 1090-1;
2.
functional tolerances required to fulfil other criteria such as fit-up and
appearance;
3.
special tolerances that may be specified for project-specific reasons, and which
would need to be clearly defined in the execution specification.
Functional tolerances are defined for two classes, of which the less onerous tolerance
class 1 is the default specification for routine execution. Tolerance class 2 is likely to
require special and more expensive measures in fabrication and erection.
As an alternative, the standard allows BS EN ISO 13920,  Welding – General tolerances
for welded constructions – Dimensions for lengths and angles – Shape and position , to be
used as the basis for specifying functional tolerances. BS EN ISO 13920 is suitable for
those weldments and more heavily welded structural components where potential
distortion from welding is the dominant factor in determining the dimensions and shape
of the completed component and its fit-up to other components. BS EN 1090-2 selects the
class relevant to the function of structural components from the four tolerance classes
defined in BS EN ISO 13920.
This publication does not purport to include all the necessary provisions of a contract.
Users are responsible for its correct application.
Compliance with a British Standard cannot confer immunity from legal
obligations.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=2>>Introduction<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This European Standard specifies requirements for execution of steel structures, in order to ensure adequate
levels of mechanical resistance and stability, serviceability and durability.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This European Standard specifies requirements for execution of steel structures in particular those that are
designed according to all parts of EN 1993 and the steel parts of composite steel and concrete structures
designed according to all parts of EN 1994.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This European Standard presupposes that the work is carried out with the necessary skill and adequate
equipment and resources to perform the work in accordance with the execution specification and the
requirements of this European Standard.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>10<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_15>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>1
Scope<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This European Standard specifies requirements for execution of structural steelwork as structures or as
manufactured components, produced from:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  hot rolled, structural steel products up to and including grade S690;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  cold formed components and sheeting up to and including grades S700 for stainless steels and including
S690 for carbon steels;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  hot finished and cold formed austenitic, austenitic-ferritic and ferritic stainless steel products;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  hot finished and cold formed structural hollow sections, including standard range and custom-made rolled
products and hollow sections manufactured by welding.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This European Standard may also be used for structural steel grades up to and including S960, provided that
conditions for execution are verified against reliability criteria and any necessary additional requirements are
specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This European Standard specifies requirements independent of the type and shape of the steel structure (e.g.
buildings, bridges, plated or latticed components) including structures subjected to fatigue or seismic actions.
The requirements are expressed in terms of execution classes<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This European Standard applies to structures designed according to the relevant part of EN 1993.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This European Standard applies to structural components and sheeting as defined in EN 1993-1-3.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This European Standard applies to steel components in composite steel and concrete structures designed
according to the relevant part of EN 1994.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This European Standard may be used for structures designed according to other design rules provided that
conditions for execution comply with them and any necessary additional requirements are specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This European Standard does not cover requirements for watertightness or air permeability resistance of
sheeting.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>11<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>3
Terms and definitions<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For the purpose of this document, the following terms and definitions apply.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>3.1
construction works
everything that is constructed or results from construction operations. This term covers both building and civil
engineering works. It refers to the complete construction comprising both structural and non-structural
components<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.2
works
parts of construction works that are structural steelwork<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.3
structural steelwork
steel structures or manufactured steel components used in construction works<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.4
constructor
person or organization executing the works (the supplier in EN ISO 9000)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.5
structure
see EN 1990<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>3.6
manufacturing
all activities required to produce and deliver a component. As relevant, this comprises e.g. procurement,
preparation and assembly, welding, mechanical fastening, transportation, surface treatment and the
inspection and documentation thereof<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>3.7
execution
all activities performed for the physical completion of the works, i.e. procurement, fabrication, welding,
mechanical fastening, transportation, erection, surface treatment and the inspection and documentation
thereof<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>3.7.1
execution specification
set of documents covering technical data and requirements for a particular steel structure including those
specified to supplement and qualify the rules of this European Standard<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 1
Execution specification includes requirements where this European Standard identifies items to be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>21<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_26>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 2
Execution specification can be seen as the complete set of requirements for manufacture and installation of
structural steel components with the manufacturing requirements given in a set of component specifications according to
prEN 1090-1.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.7.2
execution class
classified set of requirements specified for the execution of the works as a whole, of an individual component
or of a detail of a component<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.8
service category
category that characterises a component in terms of the circumstances of its use<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.9
production category
category that characterises a component in terms of the methods used for its execution<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>3.10
constituent product
material and product used for manufacturing a component and which remains as part of it, e.g. structural steel
product, stainless steel product, mechanical fastener, welding consumable<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.11
component
part of a steel structure, which may itself be an assembly of several smaller components<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.11.1
cold formed component
see EN 10079 and EN 10131<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>3.12
preparation
all activities performed on the constituent steel products to produce the parts ready for assembly and inclusion
in components. As relevant, this comprises e.g. identification, handling and storage, cutting, shaping and
holing.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.13
design basis method of erection
outline of a method of erection upon which the design of the structure is based (also known as the design
erection sequence)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.13.1
erection method statement
documentation describing the procedures to be used to erect a structure<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.14
nonconformity
see EN ISO 9000<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.15
additional NDT (non destructive testing)
NDT technique which is additional to visual examination, e.g. magnetic particle, penetrant, eddy current,
ultrasonic or radiographic testing<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.16
tolerance
see ISO 1803<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>22<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_27>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.16.1
essential tolerance
basic limits for a geometrical tolerance necessary to satisfy the design assumptions for structures in terms of
mechanical resistance and stability<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.16.2
functional tolerance
geometrical tolerance which might be required to meet a function other than mechanical resistance and
stability, e.g appearance or fit up<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>3.16.3
special tolerance
geometrical tolerance which is not covered by the tabulated types or values of tolerances given in this
European Standard, and which needs to be specified in a particular case<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.16.4
manufacturing tolerance
permitted range in the size of a dimension of a component resulting from component manufacture<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>4
Specifications and documentation<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>4.1
Execution Specification<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>4.1.1
General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The necessary information and technical requirements for execution of each part of the works shall be agreed
and complete before commencement of execution of that part of the works. There shall be procedures for
making alterations to previously agreed execution specification. Execution specification shall consider such of
the following items as are relevant:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) additional information, as listed in A.1;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) options, as listed in A.2;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) execution classes, see 4.1.2;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) preparation grades, see 4.1.3;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) tolerance classes, see 4.1.4;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f)
technical requirements regarding the safety of the works, see 4.2.3 and 9.2.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>4.1.2
Execution classes<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Four execution classes 1 to 4, denoted EXC1 to EXC4, are given, for which requirement strictness increases
from EXC1 to EXC4.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Execution classes may apply to the whole structure or to a part of the structure or to specific details. A
structure can include several execution classes. A detail or group of details will normally be ascribed one
execution class. However, the choice of an execution class does not necessarily have to be the same for all
requirements.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If no execution class is specified EXC2 shall apply.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The list of requirements related to execution classes is given in A.3.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>23<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_28>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Guidance for the choice of execution classes is given in Annex B.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
The choice of execution classes is related to production categories and service categories, with links to
consequence classes as defined in Annex B of EN 1990:2002.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>4.1.3
Preparation grades<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Three preparation grades, denoted P1 to P3 according to ISO 8501-3, are given, for which requirement
strictness increases from P1 to P3.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Preparation grades are related to the expected life of the corrosion protection and corrosivity category as
defined in Clause 10.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Preparation grades may apply to the whole structure or to a part of the structure or to specific details. A
structure can include several preparation grades. A detail or group of details will normally be ascribed one
preparation grade.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>4.1.4
Geometrical tolerances<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Two types of geometrical tolerances are defined in 11.1:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) essential tolerances;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) functional tolerances, with two classes for which requirement strictness increases from class 1 to class 2.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>4.2
Constructor's documentation<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>4.2.1
Quality documentation<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The following points shall be documented for EXC2, EXC3 and EXC4:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) the allocation of tasks and authority during the various phases of the project;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) the procedures, methods and work instructions to be applied;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) an inspection plan specific to the works;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) a procedure for handling changes and modifications;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) a procedure for handling of nonconformities, requests for concessions and quality disputes;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f)
any hold points or requirement to witness inspections or tests, and any consequent access requirements.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>4.2.2
Quality plan<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>It shall be specified if a quality plan for execution of the works is required.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
EN ISO 9000 gives the definition of a quality plan.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>It shall include:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
a general management document which shall address the following points:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>1) review of specification requirements against process capabilities;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>2) organisation chart and managerial staff responsible for each aspect of the execution;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>24<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_29>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>3) principles and organisation arrangements for inspection including allocation of responsibilities for each
inspection task;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
quality documentation prior to execution as defined in 4.2.1. The documents shall be produced before
execution of the construction step to which they relate;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c)
execution records which are actual records of inspections and checks carried out, or demonstrate
qualification or certification of implemented resources. Execution records related to a hold-point that
affect continuation of execution shall be produced before the hold-point is released.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Annex C gives a check-list for the content of a quality plan recommended for the execution of structural
steelwork with reference to the general guidelines in ISO 10005.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>4.2.3
Safety of the erection works<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Method statements giving detailed work instructions shall comply with the technical requirements relating to
the safety of the erection works as given in 9.2 and 9.3.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>4.2.4
Execution documentation<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Sufficient documentation shall be prepared during execution and as a record of the as-built structure to
demonstrate that the works have been carried out according to the execution specification.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5
Constituent products<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.1
General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Generally constituent products to be used for the execution of steel structures shall be selected from the
relevant European Standards listed in the following clauses. If constituent products that are not covered by the
standards listed are to be used, their properties shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Definitions and requirements of EN 10021 shall apply together with those of the relevant European product
standard.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.2
Identification, inspection documents and traceability<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The properties of supplied constituent products shall be documented in a way that enables them to be
compared to the specified properties. Their conformity with the relevant product standard shall be checked in
accordance with 12.2.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For metallic products, the inspection documents according to EN 10204 shall be as listed in Table 1.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>25<<HEADING_END>>

listed in Tables 2, 3 and 4, unless otherwise specified. Grades, qualities and, if appropriate, coating weights
and finishes, shall be specified together with any required options permitted by the product standard, including
those related to suitability for hot dip zinc-coating, if relevant.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Steel products to be used in the manufacture of cold formed components shall have properties that conform to
the required suitability for cold forming process. Carbon steels suitable for cold forming are listed in Table 3.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>5.3.2
Thickness tolerances<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Thickness tolerances for structural steel plates shall be as follows in accordance with EN 10029, unless
otherwise specified:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>EXC4:
Class B<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For other structural and stainless steel products the thickness class A shall be used unless otherwhise
specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.3.3
Surface conditions<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For carbon steels, surface condition requirements are as follows:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
class A2 for plates and wide flats in accordance with the requirements of EN 10163-2;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
class C1 for sections in accordance with the requirements of EN 10163-3. Execution specifications shall
specify if imperfections such as cracks, shell and seams shall be repaired.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If more stringent surface conditions are required for plates in EXC3 and EXC4, they shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For stainless steel the surface finish requirements shall be as follows:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
sheet, plate and strip: in accordance with the requirements of EN 10088-2;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
bars, rods and sections: in accordance with the requirements of EN 10088-3.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Additional requirements related to the following items: special restrictions on either surface imperfections or
repair of surface defects by grinding in accordance with EN 10163, or with EN 10088 for stainless steel, shall
be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For other products the surface finish requirements shall be specified in terms of appropriate European or
International specifications.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If the relevant specification does not adequately define decorative or specialist surface finishes, the finish shall
be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The surface condition of constituent products shall be such that the relevant requirements for surface
preparation grade in accordance with 10.2 can be achieved.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.3.4
Special properties<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For EXC3 and EXC4, internal discontinuity quality class S1 of EN 10160 shall be specified for welded
cruciform joints transmitting primary tensile stresses through the plate thickness on a band of width four times
the thickness of the plate each side of the proposed attachment.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>It shall be specified whether areas close to bearing diaphragms or stiffeners should be checked for the
existence of internal discontinuities. In this case quality class S1 of EN 10160 shall apply to a band of flange
or web plate of width 25 times the plate thickness each side of a bearing diaphragm or stiffener if attached by
welding.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>In addition, requirements related to the following items shall be specified if relevant:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
testing on constituent products, other than stainless steels, to identify internal discontinuities or cracks in
zones to be welded;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
improved deformation properties perpendicular to the surface of constituent products, other than
stainless steels, in accordance with EN 10164;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c)
special delivery conditions of stainless steels, for example Pitting Resistance Equivalent (Nitrogen)
(PRE(N)) or accelerated corrosion testing. The PRE(N) shall be given by (Cr + 3.3 Mo + 16 N), in which
the elements are in percent by weight, unless otherwise specified;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d)
processing conditions if constituent products are to be processed before delivery.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Heat treatment, cambering and bending are examples of such processes.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.4
Steel castings<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Steel castings shall conform to the requirements in EN 10340. Grades, qualities and, if appropriate, finishes
shall be specified together with any required options permitted by the product standard.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.5
Welding consumables<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>All welding consumables shall conform to the requirements to EN 13479 and the appropriate product standard
as listed in Table 5.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>29<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>The type of welding consumables shall be appropriate to the welding process, the material to be welded and
the welding procedure.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For steel grades higher than S355, the use of consumables and fluxes with medium-high basicity index is
recommended for the welding processes: 111, 114, 121, 122, 136, 137 (see 7.3 for definition of welding
processes).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If steel according to EN 10025-5 is to be welded, welding consumables shall be used which ensure that the
completed welds have a weather resistance at least equivalent to the parent metal. Unless otherwise
specified, one of the options given in Table 6 shall be used.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.6
Mechanical fasteners<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.6.1
General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The corrosion resistance of the connectors, fasteners and sealing washers shall be comparable to that
specified for the fastened components.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Hot dip galvanized coatings of fasteners shall conform to EN ISO 10684.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Protective coatings of components for mechanical fasteners shall comply with the requirements of the relevant
product standard or, in the absence thereof, with the manufacturer's recommendation.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.6.2
Terminology<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>In the text the following terms are used:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
"washer"
meaning: "plain or chamfered washer";<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
"assembly"
meaning: "a bolt with a nut and washer(s) as necessary".<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.6.3
Structural bolting assemblies for non preloaded applications<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Carbon and alloy steel and austenitic stainless steel structural bolting assemblies for non preloaded
applications shall conform to EN 15048-1.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Assemblies according to EN 14399-1 may also be used for non preloaded applications.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Property classes of bolts and nuts and, if appropriate, surface finishes shall be specified together with any
required options permitted by the product standard.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The mechanical properties shall be specified for:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
carbon and alloy steel bolting assemblies with larger diameter than those specified in
EN ISO 898-1 and EN 20898-2;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
austenitic stainless steel bolting assemblies with larger diameter than those specified in
EN ISO 3506-1 and EN ISO 3506-2;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c)
austenitic-ferritic bolts.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Fasteners according to EN ISO 898-1 and EN 20898-2 shall not be used to join stainless steels according to
EN 10088 unless otherwise specified. If insulation kits are to be used full details of their use shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.6.4
Structural bolting assemblies for preloading<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>High strength structural bolting assemblies for preloading include system HR, system HV and HRC bolts.
They shall conform to the requirements in EN 14399-1 and in the appropriate European Standard as listed in
Table 7.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Property classes of bolts and nuts and, if appropriate, surface finishes shall be specified together with any
required options permitted by the product standard.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>31<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>Bolts and nuts
Washers<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>EN 14399-3<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>EN 14399-4<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>EN 14399-5<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>EN 14399-7<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>EN 14399-6<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>EN 14399-8<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>prEN 14399-10<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Stainless steel bolts shall not be used in preloaded applications unless otherwise specified. If used they shall
be treated as special fasteners.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.6.5
Direct tension indicators<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Direct tension indicators   and associated hardened nut face and bolt face washers shall be in accordance with
prEN 14399-9.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Direct tension indicators shall not be used with weather resistant steels or stainless steels.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.6.6
Weather resistant assemblies<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Weather resistant assemblies shall be made of improved atmospheric corrosion resistance material the
chemical composition of which shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Type 3 Grade A fasteners to ASTM standard A325 would be suitable [48].<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Their mechanical characteristics, performances and delivery conditions shall conform to the requirements in
EN 14399-1 or EN 15048-1 as relevant.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.6.7
Foundation bolts<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The mechanical properties of foundation bolts shall be in accordance with EN ISO 898-1 or fabricated from
hot-rolled steel conforming to EN 10025-2 to EN 10025-4. If specified, reinforcing steels may be used. In this
case they shall conform to EN 10080 and the steel grade shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.6.8
Locking devices<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If required the locking devices such as prevailing torque nuts or other types of bolt which effectively prevent
loosening of the assembly if subjected to impact or significant vibration shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Unless otherwise specified, products from EN ISO 2320, EN ISO 7040, EN ISO 7042, EN ISO 7719, EN ISO
10511, EN ISO 10512 and EN ISO 10513 may be used.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.6.9
Taper washers<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Taper washers shall comply with the relevant product standard.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.6.10 Hot rivets<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Hot rivets shall comply with the relevant product standard.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.6.11 Fasteners for thin gauge components<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Self-drilling screws shall comply with EN ISO 15480 and self-tapping screws with EN ISO 1481,
EN ISO 7049, EN ISO 1479 or ISO 10509.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Blind rivets shall comply with EN ISO 15976, EN ISO 15979, EN ISO 15980, EN ISO 15983 or
EN ISO 15984.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Cartridge fired pins, air driven pins shall be classified as special fasteners.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Mechanical fasteners for use in stressed skin applications shall be of a specified type for such application.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.6.12 Special fasteners<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Special fasteners are fasteners that are not covered by European or International Standards. They shall be
specified, as well as any tests necessary.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
The use of special fasteners is covered in 8.9.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Hexagon injection bolts shall be classified as special fasteners.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.6.13 Delivery and identification<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Fasteners according to 5.6.3 to 5.6.5 shall be delivered and identified in accordance with the requirements of
the relevant product standard.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Fasteners according to 5.6.7 to 5.6.12 shall be delivered and identified as follows:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) They shall be delivered in an appropriate durable packaging and labelled such that the content is readily
identifiable.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) Labelling or accompanying documentation should contain the following information in a legible and
durable form:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  manufacturer’s identification and, if relevant, lot numbers;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  type of fastener and material and, if appropriate, its assembly;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  protective coating;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  dimensions in mm, as appropriate for nominal diameter and length, and if appropriate, washer diameter,
thickness and effective compression range of elastomeric part;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  size of drill bit as appropriate;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  for screws: details of the limiting torque values;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  for cartridge fired and air driven pins: details of the firing charge and driving forces as appropriate.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Fasteners and any associated washers shall bear a durable manufacturer's identification mark.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.7
Studs and shear connectors<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Studs for arc stud welding including shear connectors for steel/concrete composite construction shall comply
with the requirements of EN ISO 13918.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Shear connectors other than the stud type shall be classified as special fasteners and comply with 5.6.12.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>33<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_38>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.8
Grouting materials<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The grouting materials to be used shall be specified. It shall be cement based grout, special grout or fine
concrete.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Cement based grout for use between steel bases or bearing plates and concrete foundations shall be as
follows:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
for nominal thickness not exceeding 25 mm:
Neat Portland cement;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
for nominal thickness between 25 and 50 mm: Fluid Portland cement mortar that is not leaner than 1:1
cement to fine aggregate;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c)
for nominal thickness of 50 mm and above:
Dry as possible Portland cement mortar that is not leaner
than 1:2 cement to fine aggregate.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Special grouts include cement based grouts used with admixtures, expanding grout and resin based grout.
Those with low shrinkage characteristics are recommended.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Special grout shall be accompanied by detailed instructions for use that are attested by the manufacturer.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Fine concrete shall only be used between steel bases or bearing plates and concrete foundations that have
gaps with nominal thickness of 50 mm and above.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.9
Expansion joints for bridges<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Requirements for type and characteristics of expansion joints shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.10 High strength cables, rods and terminations<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Wires for high strength cables shall be cold drawn or cold rolled steel wires and conform to the requirements
of EN 10264-3 or EN 10264-4. The tensile strength grade and, if appropriate, coating class according to
EN 10244-2 shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Strands for high strength cables shall conform to the requirements of prEN 10138-3. The designation and
class of the strand shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Steel wire ropes shall conform to the requirements of EN 12385-1 and EN 12385-10. The minimum breaking
load and diameter of the steel wire rope and, if appropriate, requirements related to corrosion protection shall
be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The filling material for the sockets shall conform to the requirements of EN 13411-4. It shall be selected taking
into account service temperature and actions such that continued creeping of the loaded strand through the
socket is prevented.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.11 Structural bearings<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Structural bearings shall comply with the requirements of EN 1337-2, EN 1337-3, EN 1337-4,
EN 1337-5, EN 1337-6, EN 1337-7 or EN 1337-8 as relevant.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6
Preparation and assembly<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.1
General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This clause specifies the requirements for cutting, shaping, holing and assembly of constituent steel
components for inclusion into components.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>34<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_39>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE Welding and mechanical fastening are dealt with in Clauses 7 and 8.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Structural steelwork shall be fabricated considering the requirements in Clause 10 and within the tolerances
specified in Clause 11.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Equipment used in the manufacturing process shall be maintained to ensure that use, wear and failure do not
cause significant inconsistency in the manufacturing process.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.2
Identification<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>At all stages of manufacturing each piece or package of similar pieces of steel components shall be
identifiable by a suitable system. For EXC3 and EXC4 finished components shall be identified to inspection
certificates.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Identification may be achieved as appropriate by batching or by the shape and the size of the component or
by the use of durable and distinguishing marks applied in a way not producing damage. Chiselled notches are
not permitted.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The following requirements apply to hard stamped, punched or drilled marks used for marking single
components or packages of similar components, unless otherwise specified:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
they are permitted only for steel grades up to and including S355;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
they are not permitted for stainless steels;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c)
they are not permitted on coated materials for cold-formed components;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d)
they shall only be used in the specified areas where the marking method would not affect the fatigue life.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If the use of hard stamps, punched or drilled marks is not permitted, it shall be specified whether soft or low
stress stamps may be used.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Soft or low stress stamps may be used for stainless steels unless otherwise specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Any zones where identification marks are not permitted or shall not be visible after completion shall be
specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.3
Handling and storage<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Constituent products shall be handled and stored in conditions that are in accordance with product
manufacturer's recommendations.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>A constituent product shall not be used beyond a shelf life specified by its manufacturer. Products that have
been handled or stored in a way or for a length of time that could have led to significant deterioration shall be
checked before use to ensure that they still comply with the relevant product standard.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Structural steel components shall be packed, handled and transported in a safe manner, so that permanent
deformation does not occur and surface damage is minimised. Handling and storage preventive measures
specified in Table 8 shall be applied as appropriate.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>35<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_40>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Table 8 — List of handling and storage preventive measures<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Lifting<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>1
Protection of components from damage at the lifting points<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>2
Avoidance of single point lifting of long components by use of spreader beams as appropriate<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>3
Bundling together lightweight components particularly prone to edge damage, twisting and distortion if
handled as individual items. Care taken to avoid localized damage where component touch each
other, to unstiffened edges at lifting points or other zones where a significant proportion of the weight
of the bundle is imposed on a single unreinforced edge<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Storage<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>4
Stacking of manufactured components stored before transportation or erection clear of the ground to
be kept clean<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>5
Necessary supports to avoid permanent deformations<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>6
Storage of profiled sheeting, and other materials supplied with pre-finished decorative surfaces
according to the requirements of relevant standards<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Protection against corrosion<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>7
Avoidance of accumulation of water<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>8
Precautions in order to avoid the penetration of moisture into bundles of sections with metallic pre-
coatings<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
In case of prolonged open storage on site the bundles of sections should be opened and the sections
separated to avoid the occurrence of 'black or white rust'.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>9
Appropriate corrosion protection treatment of cold formed steel components less than 4 mm thick
done before leaving the manufacturing works, sufficient at least to resist the exposure likely to be
experienced during transportation, storage and initial erection<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Stainless steels<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>10
Handling and storage of stainless steel so as to prevent contamination by fixtures or manipulators etc.
Careful storage of stainless steel, so that the surfaces are protected from damage or contamination<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>11
Use of protective film or other coating, to be left on as long as practicable<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>12
Avoidance of storage in salt-laden humid atmospheres<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>13
Protection of storage racks by wooden, rubber or plastic battens or sheaths to avoid carbon steel,
copper-containing, lead etc. rubbing surfaces<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>14
Use of markers containing chloride or sulphide prohibited<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
An alternative is to use protective film and apply all marks only into this film.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>15
Protection of stainless steel from direct contact with carbon steel lifting tackle or handling equipment
such as chains, hooks, strapping and rollers or the forks of fork lift trucks by use of isolating materials
or light plywood or suction cups. Use of appropriate erection tools to ensure that surface
contamination does not occur<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>16
Avoidance of contact with chemicals, including dyes, glues, adhesive tape, undue amounts of oil and
grease<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
If it is necessary to use them, their suitability is to be checked with their manufacturer.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>17
Use of segregated manufacturing used for carbon steel and stainless steel to prevent carbon steel
pick-up. Use of separate tools dedicated for use with stainless steel only, particularly grinding wheels
and wire brushes. Wire brushes and wire wool of stainless steel, preferably an austenitic grade<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Transport<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>18
Special measures needed for protecting manufactured components in transit<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>36<<HEADING_END>>
<<TABLE_1>>
| Lifting                      |                                                                                                             |
|:-----------------------------|:------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| 1                            | Protection of components from damage at the lifting points                                                  |
| 2                            | Avoidance of single point lifting of long components by use of spreader beams as appropriate                |
| 3                            | Bundling together lightweight components particularly prone to edge damage, twisting and distortion if      |
|                              | handled as individual items. Care taken to avoid localized damage where component touch each                |
|                              | other, to unstiffened edges at lifting points or other zones where a significant proportion of the weight   |
|                              | of the bundle is imposed on a single unreinforced edge                                                      |
| Storage                      |                                                                                                             |
| 4                            | Stacking of manufactured components stored before transportation or erection clear of the ground to         |
|                              | be kept clean                                                                                               |
| 5                            | Necessary supports to avoid permanent deformations                                                          |
| 6                            | Storage of profiled sheeting, and other materials supplied with pre-finished decorative surfaces            |
|                              | according to the requirements of relevant standards                                                         |
| Protection against corrosion |                                                                                                             |
| 7                            | Avoidance of accumulation of water                                                                          |
| 8                            | Precautions in order to avoid the penetration of moisture into bundles of sections with metallic pre-       |
|                              | coatings                                                                                                    |
|                              | NOTE In case of prolonged open storage on site the bundles of sections should be opened and the sections    |
|                              | separated to avoid the occurrence of 'black or white rust'.                                                 |
| 9                            | Appropriate corrosion protection treatment of cold formed steel components less than 4 mm thick             |
|                              | done before leaving the manufacturing works, sufficient at least to resist the exposure likely to be        |
|                              | experienced during transportation, storage and initial erection                                             |
| Stainless steels             |                                                                                                             |
| 10                           | Handling and storage of stainless steel so as to prevent contamination by fixtures or manipulators etc.     |
|                              | Careful storage of stainless steel, so that the surfaces are protected from damage or contamination         |
| 11                           | Use of protective film or other coating, to be left on as long as practicable                               |
| 12                           | Avoidance of storage in salt-laden humid atmospheres                                                        |
| 13                           | Protection of storage racks by wooden, rubber or plastic battens or sheaths to avoid carbon steel,          |
|                              | copper-containing, lead etc. rubbing surfaces                                                               |
| 14                           | Use of markers containing chloride or sulphide prohibited                                                   |
|                              | NOTE An alternative is to use protective film and apply all marks only into this film.                      |
| 15                           | Protection of stainless steel from direct contact with carbon steel lifting tackle or handling equipment    |
|                              | such as chains, hooks, strapping and rollers or the forks of fork lift trucks by use of isolating materials |
|                              | or light plywood or suction cups. Use of appropriate erection tools to ensure that surface                  |
|                              | contamination does not occur                                                                                |
| 16                           | Avoidance of contact with chemicals, including dyes, glues, adhesive tape, undue amounts of oil and         |
|                              | grease                                                                                                      |
|                              | NOTE If it is necessary to use them, their suitability is to be checked with their manufacturer.            |
| 17                           | Use of segregated manufacturing used for carbon steel and stainless steel to prevent carbon steel           |
|                              | pick-up. Use of separate tools dedicated for use with stainless steel only, particularly grinding wheels    |
|                              | and wire brushes. Wire brushes and wire wool of stainless steel, preferably an austenitic grade             |

<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.4
Cutting<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.4.1
General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Cutting shall be carried out in such a way that the requirements for geometrical tolerances, maximum
hardness and smoothness of free edges as specified in this European Standard are met.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Known and recognised cutting methods are sawing, shearing, disc cutting, water jet techniques and thermal
cutting. Hand thermal cutting should be used only if it is not practical to use machine thermal cutting.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If a process does not conform, it shall not be used until corrected and checked again. It may be used on a
restricted range of constituent products that do produce conforming results.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If coated materials are to be cut, the method of cutting shall be selected to minimize the damage on the
coating.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Burrs that could cause injury or prevent the proper alignment or bedding of sections or sheeting shall be
removed.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.4.2
Shearing and nibbling<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The free edge surfaces shall be checked and smoothed as necessary in order to remove significant defects. If
grinding or machining is used after shearing or nibbling, the minimum depth of grinding or machining shall be
0,5 mm.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.4.3
Thermal cutting<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The capability of thermal cutting processes shall be periodically checked as set out below.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Four samples shall be produced from the constituent product to be cut by the process:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>1) a straight cut from the thickest constituent product;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>2) a straight cut from the thinnest constituent product;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>3) a sharp corner from a representative thickness;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>4) a curved arc from a representative thickness.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Measurements shall be taken on the straight samples over at least a 200 mm length on each and checked
against the required quality class. The sharp corner and curved samples shall be inspected to establish that
they produce edges of equivalent standard to the straight cuts.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The quality of cut surfaces defined in accordance with EN ISO 9013 shall be as follows:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
for EXC1 cut edges that are free from significant irregularities are acceptable provided that any dross is
removed. For perpendicularity or angularity tolerance, u, range 5 may be used;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
Table 9 specifies the requirements for other execution classes.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>37<<HEADING_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>6.4.4
Hardness of free edge surfaces<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For carbon steels, if specified, hardness of free edge surfaces shall be in accordance with Table 10. In this
case processes that are likely to produce local hardness (thermal cutting, shearing, punching) shall have their
capability checked. In order to achieve the required hardness of free edge surfaces, preheating of material
shall be applied as necessary.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>Unless otherwise specified, the check of the capability of the processes shall be as follows:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) four samples shall be produced from procedure tests on constituent product encompassing the range of
constituent products processed that are most susceptible to local hardening;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) four local hardness tests shall be done on each sample in locations likely to be affected. The tests shall be
in accordance with EN ISO 6507.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
The requirements for checking of hardness after welding are included in procedure testing (see 7.4.1).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.5
Shaping<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.5.1
General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Steel may be bent, pressed or forged to the required shape either by the hot or by the cold forming processes,
provided the properties are not reduced below those specified for the worked material.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Requirements and recommendations for hot, cold forming and flame straightening of steels shall be as given
in the relevant product standards and in CEN/TR 10347.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Shaping by controlled application of heat may be used under the conditions specified in 6.5.2 and 6.5.3.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Shaped components that exhibit cracking or lamellar tearing, or damage to surface coatings, shall be treated
as non conforming products.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>38<<HEADING_END>>

<<PAGE_43>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.5.2
Hot forming<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Shaping by hot forming shall conform to the requirements relating to hot forming of the relevant product
standard and to the recommendations of the steel manufacturer.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For steels according to EN 10025-4 hot forming is not permitted.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For quenched and tempered steels hot forming is not permitted unless the requirements of
EN 10025-6 are fulfilled.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Shaping by hot forming (T > 580 °C) of cold formed thin gauge components and sheeting is not permitted if
the nominal yield strength is achieved by cold forming.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For steel grades up to and including S355, the hot forming process shall take place in the red-hot state and
the temperature, timing and cooling rate shall be appropriate to the particular type of steel. Bending and
forming in the blue heat range (250 °C to 380 °C) is not permitted.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For steel grades S450+N (or +AR) according to EN 10025-2, and S420 and S460 according to
EN 10025-3, the hot forming process shall take place in the temperature range 960 °C to 750 °C with
subsequent cooling at air temperature. The cooling rate should be such as to prevent hardening as well as
excessive grain coarsening. If this is not practicable, a subsequent normalising treatment shall be carried out.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Hot forming is not allowed for S450 according to EN 10025-2 if no delivery condition is indicated.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
If no delivery condition is indicated, steel products S450 could be delivered in the thermomechanical delivery
condition.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.5.3
Flame straightening<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If distortion is to be corrected by flame straightening, this shall be undertaken by local application of heat, ensuring
that the maximum steel temperature and the cooling procedure are controlled.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For EXC3 and EXC4 a suitable procedure shall be developed. The procedure shall include at least:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) maximum  steel  temperature and procedure of cooling allowed;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)  method of  heating;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) method used for temperature measurements;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) results of mechanical tests carried out for the process approval;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e)  identification of workers  entitled to apply the process.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.5.4
Cold forming<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Shaping by cold forming, produced either by roll forming, pressing or folding shall conform to the requirements
for cold formability given in the relevant product standard. Hammering shall not be used.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Cold forming leads to reduction in the ductility. Furthermore attention is drawn to the risk of hydrogen
embrittlement associated with subsequent processes such as acid treatment during coating or hot dip galvanization.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
For steel grades higher than S355, if a stress relief treatment is carried out after cold forming, the
following two conditions shall be satisfied:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>1) temperature range: 530 °C to 580 °C;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>2) holding time: 2 min/mm of material thickness, but with a minimum time of 30 min.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>39<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_44>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Stress relief treatment at more than 580 °C, or for over an hour, may lead to deterioration of the
mechanical properties. If it is intended to stress relieve S420 to S700 steels at higher temperatures or for
longer times, the required minimum values of the mechanical properties shall be agreed in advance with
the product manufacturer.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
For stainless steels, unless otherwise specified, the minimum inside bend radii to be formed shall be:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>1) 2 t  for austenitic grades 1.4301, 1.4401, 1.4404, 1.4541 and 1.4571;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>2) 2,5 t  for austenitic-ferritic grade 1.4462.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>where t is the thickness of the material.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c)
For other grades of stainless steels, the minimum inside bend radii shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Smaller inside bend radii may be permitted if due consideration is given to issues such as steel
specification, condition and thickness and the direction of bending in relation to the rolling direction.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>In order to counteract the effects of spring-back, stainless steel needs to be over-bent to a slightly higher
degree than carbon steel.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
The power requirement for bending stainless steel are higher than for bending geometrically similar
carbon steel components, due to work hardening (by about 50% in the case of the austenitic steels or even more
in the case of 1.4462 austenitic-ferritic steel).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d)
Cold formed sections and sheeting may be shaped by cranking, smooth curving or crimping as
appropriate to the materials to be used.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For cold formed components and sheeting used as structural components, shaping by cold forming shall
comply with the following two conditions:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>1) the surface coatings and the accuracy of profile shall not be impaired;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>2) It shall be specified if constituent products require protective membranes to be applied before forming.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 1 Some coatings and finishes are particularly prone to abrasive damage, both during forming and
subsequently during erection. For further information, see EN 508-1 and EN 508-3.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Bending by cold forming of hollow section components may be used provided that hardness and
geometry of the as-bent constituent product are checked.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 2 Bending by cold forming may cause alteration of section properties (e.g. concavity, ovality and wall
thinning) and increased hardness.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e)
For circular tubes bending by cold forming shall comply with the following three conditions, unless
otherwise specified:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>1) the ratio of the overall diameter of the tube to the wall thickness shall not exceed 15;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>2) the bend radius (at the centreline of the tube) shall not be less than 1,5d or d+100 mm, whichever is
the larger, in which d is the overall diameter of the tube;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>3)  welded joint in the cross-section shall be positioned close to the neutral axis, in order to reduce the
bending stresses at the weld .<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>40<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>6.6
Holing<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.6.1
Dimensions of holes<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This clause applies to the making of holes for connections with mechanical fasteners and pins.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The definition of the nominal hole diameter combined with the nominal diameter of the bolt to be used in the
hole determines whether the hole is "normal" or "oversize". The terms "short" and "long" applied to slotted
holes refer to two types of holes used for the structural design of preloaded bolts. These terms may be used
also to designate clearances for non-preloaded bolts. Special dimensions should be specified for movement
joints.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The nominal clearances for bolts and for pins not intended to act in fitted conditions shall be as specified in
Table 11. The nominal clearance is defined as:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  the difference between the nominal hole diameter and the nominal bolt diameter for round holes;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  the difference between respectively the length or the width of the hole and the nominal bolt diameter for
slotted holes.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Table 11 — Nominal clearances for bolts and pins (mm)<<HEADING_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>a     For applications such as towers and masts the nominal clearance for normal round holes shall be reduced by 0,5 mm
unless otherwise specified.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>b    For coated fasteners, 1 mm nominal clearance can be increased by the coating thickness of the fastener.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>c    Bolts with nominal diameter 12 and 14 mm, or countersunk bolts may also be used in 2 mm clearance holes under conditions
given in EN 1993-1-8.<<HEADING_END>>

for normal round holes.<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For fit bolts the nominal hole diameter shall be equal to the shank diameter of the bolt.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 1 For fit bolts to EN 14399-8 the nominal diameter of the shank is 1 mm larger than nominal diameter of the
threaded portion.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For hot rivets the nominal hole diameter shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For countersunk bolts or hot rivets, nominal dimensions of the countersinking and tolerances on those shall be
such that after installation the bolt or rivet shall be flush with the outer face of the outer ply. The dimensions of
the countersinking shall be specified accordingly. If countersinking through more than one ply the plies shall
be held firmly together during countersinking.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If countersunk bolts are identified as being for use in tension or preloaded applications, the nominal depth of
countersinking shall be at least 2 mm less than the nominal thickness of the outer ply.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 2
The 2 mm is to allow for adverse tolerances.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>6.6.2
Tolerances on hole diameter for bolts and pins<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Unless otherwise specified, hole diameters shall comply with the following:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) holes for fit bolts and fitted pins:
class H11 according to ISO 286-2;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) other holes:
± 0,5 mm, the hole diameter being taken as the average of entry and
exit diameters (see Figure 1).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.6.3
Execution of holing<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Holes for fasteners or pins may be formed by any process (drilling, punching, laser, plasma or other thermal
cutting) provided that this leaves a finished hole such that:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
cutting requirements relating to local hardness and quality of cut surface, according to 6.4 are fulfilled;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
all matching holes for fasteners or pins register with each other so that fasteners can be inserted freely
through the assembled members in a direction at right angles to the faces in contact.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Punching is permitted provided that the nominal thickness of the component is not greater than the nominal
diameter of the hole, or for a non-circular hole, its minimum dimension.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For EXC1 and EXC2, holes may be formed by punching without reaming unless otherwise specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>-
For EXC3 and EXC4, punching without reaming is not permitted. The holes shall be punched at least 2
mm undersize in diameter.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>-
The capability of holing processes shall be checked periodically as follows:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>-
eight samples shall be produced from procedure tests on constituent product encompassing the
range of hole diameters, constituent product thickness and grades processed;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>-
hole sizes shall be checked at both ends of each hole using go/no go gauges. Holes shall comply
with the tolerance class as specified in 6.6.2.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If the process does not conform it shall not be used until corrected. It may be used on a restricted range of
constituent products and hole sizes that do produce conforming results.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Holes shall also conform to the following:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>1) the taper angle ( α ) shall not exceed that shown in Figure 1;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>2) the burrs ( ∆ ) shall not exceed that shown in Figure 1;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>3) at splices, the holes in mating surfaces shall be punched in one direction in all components.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

(
min

d
d
D<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>max  (∆ 1  or  ∆ 2 )  ≤  max (D/10 ; 1 mm)<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>α   ≤   4° (i.e. 7 %);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Figure 1 — Permitted distortions of punched holes and plasma cuts<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Holes for fit bolts and fit pins may be either drilled full size or reamed in situ. If the holes are to be reamed in
situ, they shall be made at least 3 mm undersized initially by drilling or punching. If the fastener is to fit through
multiple plies they shall be held firmly together during drilling or reaming. The reaming shall be carried out with
a fixed spindle device. Acidic lubricant shall not be used.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Countersinking of normal round holes for countersunk bolts or rivets shall be undertaken after holing.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Long slotted holes shall be either punched in one operation or formed by drilling or punching two holes and
completed by hand thermal cutting, unless otherwise specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For cold formed components and sheeting, slotted holes may be formed by punching in a single operation,
consecutive punching, or joining two punched or drilled holes by use of a jig saw.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Burrs shall be removed from holes before assembly. If holes are drilled in one operation through parts
clamped together which would not otherwise be separated after drilling, removing of burrs is necessary only
from the outside holes.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.7
Cut outs<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Over-cutting of re-entrant corners shall not be permitted. Re-entrant corners are those where the open angle
between the faces is less than 180°.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Re-entrant corners and notches shall be rounded off with a minimum radius of:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  5 mm for EXC2 and EXC3.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  10 mm for EXC4.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Examples are given in Figure 2.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>43<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>

[Image 2 contains text: Se]

not permitted
2
Form A (recommended for fully mechanised or automatic cutting)
