<<HEADING level=3>>Figure 2 — Example of cut outs<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>At punched cut outs in plates over 16 mm in thickness, the deformed materials shall be removed by grinding.
Punched cut outs are not permitted for EXC4.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For thin gauge components and sheeting, locations where sharp re-entrant corners are not permitted shall be
specified with the minimum acceptable radii.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.8
Full contact bearing surfaces<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If full contact bearing surfaces are specified, the cutting length, squareness of ends and flatness of surface
shall comply with the tolerances specified in Clause 11.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.9
Assembly<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Assembly of components shall be carried out so as to fulfil the specified tolerances.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Precautions shall be taken so as to prevent galvanic corrosion produced by contact between different metallic
materials.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Contamination of stainless steel by contact with structural steel should be avoided.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Drifting to align holes shall be carried out in such a way that the elongation does not exceed the values given
in D.2.8 No 6 as follows:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  EXC1 and EXC2: Class 1;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  EXC3 and EXC4: Class 2.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>In case those values are exceeded holes shall be corrected by reaming.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Holes for which elongation is not permitted shall be identified and not be used for alignment (e.g. for fit bolts).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
In such cases specific alignment holes may be provided.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>All connections for temporary components provided for manufacturing purposes shall meet the requirements
of this European Standard and any special requirements including those related to fatigue which shall be
specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Requirements for camber or presets in components shall be checked after completion of assembly.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>44<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_49>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.10 Assembly check<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The fit between manufactured components that are inter-connected at multiple connection interfaces shall be
checked using dimensional templates, accurate three-dimensional measurements or by trial assembly.
Requirements for whether, and to what extent, trial assembly is to be used shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Trial assembly means putting together sufficient components of a whole structure to check that they fit. It
should be considered to prove fit-up between components if this is not provable by using templates or
measurement.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7
Welding<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.1
General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Welding shall be undertaken in accordance with the requirements of the relevant part of EN ISO 3834 or
EN ISO 14554 as applicable.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Guidelines for implementation of EN ISO 3834 on quality requirements for fusion welding of metallic materials
is given in CEN ISO/TR 3834-6. [29]<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>According to the execution class, the following parts of EN ISO 3834 apply:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  EXC1:
Part 4 "Elementary quality requirements";<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  EXC2:
Part 3 "Standard quality requirements";<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  EXC3 and EXC4: Part 2 "Comprehensive quality requirements".<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Arc welding of ferritic steels and stainless steels should follow the requirements and recommendations of
EN 1011-1, EN 1011-2, EN 1011-3 as amended in 7.7.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.2
Welding plan<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.2.1
Requirements for a welding plan<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>A welding plan shall be provided as part of the production planning required by the relevant part of
EN ISO 3834.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.2.2
Content of a welding plan<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Implementation of the welding plan shall include, as relevant:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
the welding procedure specifications including welding consumable, any preheating, interpass
temperature and post weld heat treatment requirements;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
measures to be taken to avoid distortion during and after welding;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c)
the sequence of welding with any restrictions or acceptable locations for start and stop positions,
including intermediate stop and start positions where joint geometry is such that welding cannot be
executed continuously;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Guidance for joints of hollow sections is given in Annex E.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d)
requirements for intermediate checking;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e)
turning of components in the welding process, in connection with the sequence of welding;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>45<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_50>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f)
details of restraints to be applied;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>g)
measures to be taken to avoid lamellar tearing;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>h)
special equipment for welding consumables (low hydrogen, conditioning etc.);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>i)
weld profile and finish for stainless steels;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>j)
requirements for acceptance criteria of welds in accordance with 7.6;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>k)
cross reference to 12.4 of the inspection and test plan;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>l)
requirements for weld identification;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>m)
requirements for surface treatment according to Clause 10.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If welding or assembly overlaps or masks previous welds special consideration is needed concerning which
welds are to be executed first and the possible need to inspect/test a weld before the second weld is executed
or before masking components are assembled.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>121: Submerged arc welding with one wire electrode;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>122: Submerged arc welding with strip electrode;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>123: Submerged arc welding with multiple wire electrodes;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>124: Submerged arc welding with metallic powder addition;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>125: Submerged arc welding with tubular electrodes;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>131: Metal inert gas welding; MIG-welding;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>135: Metal active gas welding; MAG-welding;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>136: Tubular-cored arc welding with active gas shield;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>137

testing according to EN ISO 10447.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Other welding processes shall only be used if explicitly specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.4
Qualification of welding procedures and welding personnel<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.4.1
Qualification of welding procedures<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.4.1.1
General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Welding shall be carried out with qualified procedures using a welding procedure specification (WPS) in
accordance with the relevant part of EN ISO 15609 or EN ISO 14555 or EN ISO 15620, as relevant. If
specified, special deposition conditions for tack welds shall be included in the WPS. For joints in hollow
section lattice structures the WPS shall define the start and stop zones and the method to be used in order to
cope with locations where the welds change from a fillet weld to butt around a joint.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.4.1.2
Qualification of welding procedures for processes 111, 114, 12, 13 and 14<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
The qualification of the welding procedure depends on the execution class, the parent metal and the
degree of mechanization in accordance with Table 12.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
If EN ISO 15613 or EN ISO 15614-1 qualification procedures are used, the following conditions apply:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>1) If impact tests are specified, they shall be carried out at the lowest temperature for which the standard
of the steel grade requires impact properties.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>2) For steels according to EN 10025-6, one specimen for micro-examination is necessary. Photographs
of weld metal, fusion line zone and HAZ shall be recorded. Microcracks are not permitted.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>3) If welding on shop primers, tests shall be carried out on the maximum (nominal + tolerance) accepted
layer thickness.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c)
If a qualification procedure is to apply to transverse stressed fillet welds on steel grades higher than
S275, test shall be completed by a cruciform tensile test performed in accordance with
EN ISO 9018. Only specimens with  a   ≤  0,5  t  shall be evaluated. Three cross tensile specimen shall be
tested. If the fracture happens in the parent metal, the minimum nominal tensile strength of the parent
metal shall be reached. If the fracture happens in the weld metal, the fracture strength of the cross
section of the actual weld shall be determined. By processes with deep penetration the actual root
penetration shall be considered. The determined average fracture strength shall be  ≥  0,8  R m  (with  R m  =
nominal tensile strength of the used parent metal).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

EN ISO 10447.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.4.2
Welders and welding operators<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Welders shall be qualified in accordance with EN 287-1 and welding operators in accordance with
EN 1418.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Welding hollow section branch connection with angles less than 60° shall be qualified by specific test.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Records of all welder and welding operator qualification tests shall be kept available.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.4.3
Welding coordination<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For EXC2, EXC3 and EXC4, welding coordination shall be maintained during the execution of welding by
welding coordination personnel suitably qualified for, and experienced in the welding operations they
supervise as specified in EN ISO 14731.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>With respect to the welding operations being supervised, welding coordination personnel shall have a
technical knowledge according to Tables 14 and 15.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 1
Steel groups are those defined in ISO/TR 15608. Correspondence to steel grades and reference standards
can be found in ISO/TR 20172.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 2
B, S and C are respectively basic, specific and comprehensive knowledge as specified in
EN ISO 14731.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>7.5
Preparation and execution of welding<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.5.1
Joint preparation<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.5.1.1
General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Joint preparation shall be appropriate for the welding process. If qualification of welding procedures is
performed in accordance with EN ISO 15614-1, EN ISO 15612 or EN ISO 15613 joint preparation shall
comply with the type of preparation used in the welding procedure test. Tolerances for joints preparations and
fit-up shall be given in the WPSs.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 1
EN ISO 9692-1 and EN ISO 9692-2 give some recommended weld preparation details. For weld preparation
details of bridge decks, see EN 1993-2:2006, Annex C.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Joint preparation shall be free from visible cracks. For steel grades higher than S460, cut areas shall be
descaled by grinding, and verified to be free from cracks by visual inspection, dye penetrant or magnetic
particle testing. Visible cracks shall be removed by grinding and the joint geometry corrected as necessary.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If large notches or other errors in joint geometry are corrected by welding a qualified procedure shall be used,
and the area shall be subsequently ground smooth and feathered into the adjacent surface.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>All surfaces to be welded shall be dry and free from material that would adversely affect the quality of the
welds or impede the process of welding (rust, organic material or galvanizing).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Prefabrication primers (shop primers) may be left on the fusion faces only if they do not adversely affect the
welding process. For EXC3 and EXC4, prefabrication primers shall not be left on the fusion faces, unless
welding procedure tests in accordance with EN ISO 15614-1 or EN ISO 15613 have been completed using
such prefabrication primers.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 2
EN ISO 17652-2 describes tests for assessing the influence of shop primers on the weldability.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>51<<HEADING_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.5.1.2
Hollow sections<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Circular hollow sections being used as branch components in fillet welded joints may be cut in straight
segments to prepare them for interconnection at saddle joints provided that the fit-up of the joint geometry
suits the requirements of the WPS.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For joints between hollow sections welded from one side, the joint preparations given EN ISO 9692-1 and EN
ISO
9692-2
shall
be
used,
as
appropriate.
Annex
E
illustrates
the
application
given
in
EN ISO 9692-1 and EN ISO 9692-2 to branch joints between hollow sections.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For branch connections in hollow section lattice structures, any adjustment for lack of fit by a welded surface
deposit shall be covered by a suitable welding procedure.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.5.2
Storage and handling of welding consumables<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The welding consumables shall be stored, handled and used in accordance with the manufacturer's
recommendations.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If electrodes and fluxes need to be dried and stored, appropriate temperature levels and times shall be fulfilled
in accordance with the manufacturer's recommendations or, if not available, with the requirements of Table
16.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Table 16 — Temperature and time for drying and storage of welding consumables<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Temperature level (T)
Time (t)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Drying  a
300 °C< T  ≤  400 °C
2 h < t  ≤  4 h<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Storage  a
≥  150 °C
prior to welding<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Storage  b
≥  100 °C
during welding<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a    Fixed oven
b    Portable quiver<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Consumables remaining unused at the end of the welding shift shall be dried again in accordance with the
above requirements. For electrodes, drying shall be carried out no more than twice. Remaining consumables
shall be discarded.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Welding consumables showing signs of damage or deterioration shall be rejected.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Examples of damage or deterioration include cracked or flaked coatings on covered electrodes, rusty or dirty
electrode wires and electrode wires with flaked or damaged copper coatings.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.5.3
Weather protection<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Both the welder and the working area shall be adequately protected against the effects of wind, rain and
snow.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Gas shielded welding processes are particularly sensitive to wind effects.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Surfaces to be welded shall be maintained dry and free from condensation.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If the temperature of material to be welded is below 5 °C suitable heating might be necessary.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For steel grades higher than S355 suitable heating shall be provided if the temperature of the material is
below 5 °C.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

| Drying a                       | 300 °C< T ≤ 400 °C      | 2 h < t ≤ 4 h    |
| Storage a                      | ≥ 150 °C                | prior to welding |
| Storage b                      | ≥ 100 °C                | during welding   |
| a Fixed oven b Portable quiver |                         |                  |

<<PAGE_57>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.5.4
Assembly for welding<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Components to be welded shall be brought into alignment and held in position by tack welds or external
devices and maintained during initial welding. Assembly shall be carried out such that the fit-up of joints and
the final dimensions of the components are all within the specified tolerances. Suitable allowances shall be
made for distortion and shrinkage.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The components to be welded shall be assembled and held in position such that the joints to be welded are
readily accessible and easily visible to the welder.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Assembly of hollow section components to be welded should be in accordance with the guidance given in
Annex E, unless otherwise specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Additional welds shall not be introduced, and the locations of specified welds shall not be changed without
ensuring compliance with the specification. Methods of locally strengthening a welded joint in a hollow section
lattice structure should facilitate the testing of the integrity of the as-welded joint. The alternative of thickening
the component should also be considered.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Typical details include saddles, diaphragms, division plates, cover plates, cheek plates and through plates.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.5.5
Preheating<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Preheating shall be carried out in accordance with EN ISO 13916 and EN 1011-2.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Preheat shall be undertaken according to applicable WPS and applied during welding, including tack welding
and the welding of temporary attachments.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.5.6
Temporary attachments<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If the assembly or erection procedure requires the use of components temporarily attached by welds, they
shall be positioned such that they can easily be removed without damage to the permanent steelwork. All
welds for temporary attachments shall be made in accordance with the WPS. Any areas where welding of
temporary attachments is not permitted shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The use of temporary attachments for EXC3 and EXC4 shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If temporary welded attachments have to be removed by cutting or chipping, the surface of the parent metal
shall subsequently be carefully ground smooth. Cutting and chipping are not permitted for EXC3 and EXC4,
unless otherwise specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Adequate inspection shall be carried out to ensure that the constituent product is not cracked on the surface at
the temporary weld location.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.5.7
Tack welds<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For EXC2, ECX3 and EXC4, tack welds shall be made using a qualified welding procedure. The minimum
length of the tack shall be the lesser of four times the thickness of the thicker part or 50 mm, unless a shorter
length can be demonstrated as satisfactory by test.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>All tack welds not incorporated into the final welds shall be removed. Tack welds that are to be incorporated
into the final weld shall have a suitable shape and be carried out by qualified welders. Tack welds shall be free
from deposition faults and shall be cleaned thoroughly before final welding. Cracked tack welds shall be
removed.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>53<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_58>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.5.8
Fillet welds<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.5.8.1
General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>A fillet weld, as deposited, shall not be less than the specified dimensions for throat thickness and/or leg
length as appropriate, taking into account the following:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) the full throat thickness shown as achievable using WPSs for deep or partial penetration welding
processes;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) that if a gap  h  exceeds the imperfection limit, it may be compensated for by an increase in the throat
thickness  a  =  a nom  + 0,7 h  where  a nom  is the specified nominal throat thickness. For "Incorrect fit up" (617)
quality levels apply provided that the throat thickness is maintained in accordance with (5213);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) that for bridge decks particular manufacturing requirements apply, e.g. for the throat thickness of fillet
welds, see 7.5.18 and D.2.16.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.5.8.2
Fillet welds for thin gauge components<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Fillet welds terminating at the ends or sides of thin gauge components shall be returned continuously around
the corners for a distance of not less than twice the leg length of the weld unless access or configuration
renders this impracticable. End returns on fillet welds shall be completed unless otherwise specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The minimum length of a run of fillet weld, excluding end returns, shall be at least four times the leg length of
the weld.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Intermittent fillet weld shall not be used where capillary action could lead to the formation of rust pockets. End
runs of fillet welds shall extend to the end of the part connected.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For lap joints, the minimum lap shall be not less than four times the thickness of the thinner connected part.
Single fillet welds shall not be used if the parts are not restrained to prevent opening of the joint.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If the end of a component is connected only by longitudinal fillet welds, the length of each weld shall not be
less than the transverse spacing between them.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.5.9
Butt welds<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.5.9.1
General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The location of butt welds used as splices to accommodate available lengths of constituent products shall be
checked for consistency with design.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The ends of butt welds shall be terminated in a manner that ensures sound welds with full throat thickness.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For EXC3 and EXC4, and for EXC2 if specified, run-on/run-off pieces shall be used to ensure full throat
thickness at the edge. The weldability of such run-on/run-off pieces shall not be less than that of the parent
metal.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>After completion of the welds, any run-on/run-off pieces or supplementary material shall be removed and their
removal shall comply with 7.5.6.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If a flush surface is required, the excess weld metal shall be removed to satisfy the quality requirements.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.5.9.2
Single sided welds<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Full penetration welds welded from one side may be produced with or without metallic or non metallic backing
material.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>54<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_59>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Unless otherwise specified, permanent steel backing material may be used. The requirements for its use shall
be included in the WPS.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If steel backing is used, it shall have a carbon equivalent value (CEV) not exceeding 0,43 %, or be the same
material as the most weldable of the parent metal to be joined by the weld.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Backing materials shall be fitted tightly to the parent metal and should generally be continuous for the full
length of the joint. For EXC3 and EXC4, permanent backing metal shall be made continuous by means of full
penetration butt welds. Tack welds shall be included in the butt welds.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Flush grinding of single-sided butt welds in joints between hollow sections executed without backing is not
permitted, unless otherwise specified; if those welds are fully backed they may be ground off flush with the
general surface profile of the parent metal.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.5.9.3
Back gouging<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Back gouging shall be carried out to a sufficient depth to ensure full penetration into the previously deposited
weld metal.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Back gouging shall produce a contour of a single U-shaped groove with its fusion faces readily accessible for
welding.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.5.10 Welds on steels with improved atmospheric corrosion resistance<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Welds on steels with improved atmospheric resistance shall be carried out using appropriate welding
consumables (see Table 6). As a further option, C-Mn consumables may be used for the body of a multi-run
fillet or butt weld provided the capping runs are made using suitable consumables.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.5.11 Branch connections<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Branch connections in hollow section lattice structures, which use combined welded joints (fillet weld and
single-sided butt weld), may be welded without backing.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If the bracing angle at the toe of hollow section branch connection is less than 60°, the toe shall be bevelled to
permit a butt weld to be used.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Recommendations for execution of branch connections are given in Annex E.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.5.12 Stud welding<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Stud welding shall be carried out in accordance with EN ISO 14555.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.5.13 Slot and plug welds<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Holes for slot and plug welds shall be proportioned so that adequate access can be provided for welding.
Dimensions shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Suitable dimensions are:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
width: at least 8 mm more than the thickness of the part containing it;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
length of elongated hole: the lesser of 70 mm or five times the plate thickness.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Plug welds shall be made only on slot welds after the fillet welding in the slot has been checked as
satisfactory. Plug welds performed without previous slot welding are not permitted unless otherwise specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>55<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_60>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.5.14 Spot welds for thin gauge components<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.5.14.1
Arc spot welds<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Weld washers should have a thickness of between 1,2 mm and 2,0 mm with a pre-punched hole of
10 mm minimum diameter.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For stainless steels weld washers are accepted only if specified and according to the service conditions.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 1
Weld washers can introduce crevices into the joint; the acceptability of these crevices depends on the service
conditions.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The minimum visible width,  d w , of a circular arc spot weld, or an elongated arc spot weld shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 2
Guidance on the relationship between the interface dimension and the visible width of a circular arc spot weld
or an elongated arc spot weld is given in EN 1993-1-3<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.5.14.2
Resistance spot welds<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The diameter of a resistance spot weld should correspond as closely as practicable to the recommended tip
diameter of the electrode  d r  (in mm), given by  d r  = 5  t 1/2<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>where<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>t
is the thickness of the sheet in contact with the electrode tip (in mm).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.5.15 Other weld types<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The requirements for other weld types, e.g. seal welds, shall be specified and shall be subject to the same
welding requirements as specified in this European Standard.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.5.16 Post-weld heat treatment<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If heat treatment of welded components is necessary, it shall be demonstrated that the procedures used are
appropriate.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Guidance for quality requirements for heat treatment is given in ISO/TR 17663.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.5.17 Execution of welding<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Precautions shall be taken to avoid stray arcing, and if stray arc do occur the surface of the steel shall be
lightly ground and checked. Visual checking should be supplemented by penetrant or magnetic particle
testing.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Precautions shall be taken to avoid weld spatter. For EXC3 and EXC4, it shall be removed.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Visible imperfections such as cracks, cavities and other not permitted imperfections shall be removed from
each run before deposition of further runs.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>All slag shall be removed from the surface of each run before each subsequent run is added and from the
surface of the finished weld. Particular attention shall be paid to the junctions between the weld and the parent
metal.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Any requirements for grinding and dressing of the surface of completed welds shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>56<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_61>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.5.18 Welding of bridge decks<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Production tests shall be carried out according to 12.4.4 c). Production tests are not required for stiffener-deck
plate connection outside the roadway (kerbs) which is without loading by vehicles.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For stiffener-deck plate connections and local welds, e.g. at stiffener-stiffener connections with splice plates
the starts and stops shall be removed.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For stiffener-crossbeam connections with stiffeners passing through the crossbeam with or without cope holes
at first the stiffeners should be welded to the deck plate and the crossbeams subsequently assembled and
welded.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.6
Acceptance criteria<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Welded components shall comply with the requirements specified in Clauses 10 and 11.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The acceptance criteria for weld imperfections shall be as follows, with reference to EN ISO 5817, except
"Incorrect toe" (505) and "Micro lack of fusion" (401) which are not to be taken into account. Any additional
requirements specified for weld geometry and profile shall be taken into account.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  EXC1
quality level D;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  EXC2
generally quality level C except quality level D for "Undercut" (5011, 5012), "Overlap" (506),
"Stray arc" (601) and "End crater pipe" (2025);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  EXC3
quality level B;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  EXC4
quality level B+ which is quality level B with the additional requirements given in
Table 17.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>  Clause 19 — Addition:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Welding procedure qualification records and associated WPSs that do not include a thermal efficiency
factor in a heat input calculation may be used provided the heat input is adjusted in accordance with the
appropriate thermal efficiency factor.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.7.2
Amendments to EN 1011-3 requirements<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  7.1, Paragraph 4 — Modification:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The required surface finish of the weld zones shall be specified. It shall be specified if the coloured oxide
films formed during welding shall be removed. Due consideration should be given to corrosion
resistance, environment, aesthetics and the implications of dressing off and cleaning the weld zone. All
slag associated with welding shall be removed unless otherwise specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
The discolouration of the weld zone after welding is influenced by the amount of oxygen in the “backing
gas” during welding. Coloured photographic reference scales are available to assist with specifying acceptable
discolouration [49].<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  7.1, Paragraph 5 — Modification:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>After preparation of joint faces, oxidation, hardening and general contamination from thermal cutting
processes may need to be eliminated by mechanically machining to a sufficient depth from the cut face.
During shearing cracking may occur; these cracks shall be removed prior to welding.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  7.3, Paragraph 3 — Addition at the beginning of the paragraph:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Copper backing shall not be used unless otherwise specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  Clause 10 — Addition:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Appropriate care shall be taken in the disposal of all post weld cleaning materials.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  A.1.2, Paragraph 1 — Modification to last sentence:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The approximate microstructure, which will form in the weld metal, may be indicated from the balance of
ferrite and austenite stabilizing elements using a Schaeffler, DeLong, W.R.C. or Espy diagram. If used,
the appropriate diagram shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  A.2.2, Paragraph 4 — Modification:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The Schaeffler, DeLong, W.R.C. or Espy diagrams may be used to indicate if the consumable will
provide the correct ferrite content, taking dilution effects into account. If used, the appropriate diagram
shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  A.4.1 — Addition:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Welded connections shall not be subject to heat treatment after welding unless permitted by
specification.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  C.4. — Addition:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Welded connections shall not be subject to heat treatment after welding unless permitted by
specification.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.7.3
Welding dissimilar steels<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The requirements for welding different stainless steel types to each other or to other steels, such as carbon
steels, shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The welding coordinator shall take into account the appropriate welding techniques, welding processes and
welding consumables. The issues associated with contamination of the stainless steel and galvanic corrosion
should be considered carefully.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>8
Mechanical fastening<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>8.1
General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This clause covers requirements for shop and site fastening including the fixing of profiled sheeting.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Separate components forming part of a common ply shall not differ in thickness by more than D, where D is
2 mm generally and 1 mm in preloaded applications, see Figure 3. If steel packing plates are provided to
ensure that the difference in thickness does not exceed the above limit, their thickness shall not be less than
2 mm.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>In case of severe exposure, avoiding cavity corrosion may require closer contact.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Plate thickness shall be chosen to limit the number of packing plates to a maximum of three.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<IMAGE_3>>
[Image 3 contains text: —— ee]
<<HEADING level=3>>Figure 3 — Difference of thickness between components of a common ply<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Packing plates shall have compatible corrosion behaviour and mechanical strength with the adjacent plate
components of the connection. Full consideration shall be given to the risk and implication of galvanic
corrosion resulting from dissimilar metals being in contact.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>8.2
Use of bolting assemblies<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>8.2.1
General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This clause refers to bolting assemblies specified in 5.6, consisting of matching bolts, nuts and washers (as
necessary).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>It shall be specified if, in addition to tightening, other measures or means are to be used to secure the nuts.<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Bolted connections with small clamp lengths in thin gauge components subject to significant vibrations, such
as storage racks, shall use a locking method.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Preloaded assemblies do not need additional locking devices.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Bolts and nuts shall not be welded, unless otherwise specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>60<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_65>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
This does not apply to special weld nuts according to e.g. EN ISO 21670 or weld studs.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>8.2.2
Bolts<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The nominal fastener diameter used for structural bolting shall be at least M 12, unless otherwise specified
together with the associated requirements. For thin gauge components and sheeting the minimum diameter
shall be specified for each type of fastener.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The bolt length shall be chosen such that after tightening the following requirements are met for bolt end
protrusion beyond the nut face and the thread length.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The length of protrusion shall be at least the length of one thread pitch measured from the outer face of the
nut to the end of the bolt.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If it is intended that a connection utilises the shear capacity of the unthreaded shank of bolts, then the
dimensions of the bolts shall be specified to allow for the tolerances on the length of the unthreaded portion.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
The length of the unthreaded bolt shaft of full cross section is shorter than the nominal unthreaded length (e.g. by
up to 12mm for an M20 bolt).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For non-preloaded bolts, at least one full thread (in addition to the thread run out) shall remain clear between
the bearing surface of the nut and the unthreaded part of the shank.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For preloaded bolts according to EN 14399-3 and EN 14399-7, at least four full threads (in addition to the
thread run out) shall remain clear between the bearing surface of the nut and the unthreaded part of the
shank.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For preloaded bolts according to EN 14399-4 and EN 14399-8, clamp lengths shall be in accordance with
those specified in Table A.1 of EN 14399-4:2005.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>8.2.3
Nuts<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Nuts shall run freely on their partnering bolt, which is easily checked during hand assembly. Any nut and bolt
assembly where the nut does not run freely shall be discarded. If a power tool is used, either of the following
two checks may be used:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
for each new batch of nuts or bolts their compatibility may be checked by hand assembly before
installation;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
for mounted bolt assemblies but prior to tightening, sample nuts may be checked for free-running by
hand after initial loosening.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Nuts shall be assembled so that their designation markings are visible for inspection after assembly.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>8.2.4
Washers<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Generally washers are not required for use with non-preloaded bolts in normal round holes. If required, it shall
be specified whether washers are to be placed under the nut or the bolt head, whichever is rotated, or both.
For single lap connections with only one bolt row, washers are required under both bolt head and the nut.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
The use of washers can reduce local damage to metal coatings particularly where these are thick coatings.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Washers used under heads of preloaded bolts shall be chamfered according to EN 14399-6 and positioned
with the chamfer towards the bolt head. Washers according to EN 14399-5 shall only be used under nuts.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>61<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_66>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Plain washers (or if necessary hardened taper washers) shall be used for preloaded bolts as follows:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
for 8.8 bolts a washer shall be used under the bolt head or the nut, whichever is to be rotated;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
for 10.9 bolts washers shall be used under both the bolt head and the nut.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Plate washers shall be used for connections with long slotted and oversized holes. One additional plate
washer or up to three washers with a maximum combined thickness of 12 mm may be used in order to adjust
the grip length of bolt assemblies. They shall be placed on the side that is not turned.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Dimensions and steel grades of plate washers shall be specified. They shall not be thinner than 4 mm.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Taper washers shall be used if the surface of the constituent product is at an angle to a plane perpendicular to
the bolt axis of more than:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) 1/20 (3°) for bolts with  d   ≤  20 mm;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) 1/30 (2°) for bolts with  d  > 20 mm.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Dimensions and steel grades of taper washers shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>8.3
Tightening of non-preloaded bolts<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The connected components shall be drawn together such that they achieve firm contact. Shims may be used
to
adjust
the
fit.
For
constituent
products
with
t
≥
4 mm
for
plates
and
sheeting
and
t   ≥  8 mm for sections, unless full contact bearing is specified, residual gaps of up to 4 mm may be left at the
edges on condition that contact bearing is achieved at the central part of a connection.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Each bolt assembly shall be brought at least to a snug-tight condition, with special care being given to avoid
over-tightening especially short bolts and M12. The tightening process shall be carried out from bolt to bolt of
the group, starting from the most rigid part of the connection and moving progressively towards the least rigid
part. To achieve a uniform snug-tight condition, more than one cycle of tightening may be necessary.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 1
The most rigid part of a cover plate connection of an  I  section is commonly in the middle of the connection bolt
group. The most rigid parts of end plate connections of  I  sections are usually beside the flanges.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 2
The term "snug-tight" can generally be taken as that achievable by the effort of one man using a normal sized
spanner without an extension arm, and can be set as the point at which a percussion wrench starts hammering.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The bolt shall protrude from the face of the nut after tightening not less than one full thread pitch.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>8.4
Preparation of contact surfaces in slip resistant connections<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This clause is not applicable to stainless steels for which any requirement related to contact surfaces shall be
specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This clause does not deal with corrosion protection for which requirements are specified in Clause 10 and
Annex F.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The area of contact surfaces in preloaded connections shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The contact surfaces shall be prepared to produce the required slip factor which shall generally be determined
by test as specified in Annex G.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>62<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_67>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The following precautions shall be taken prior to assembly:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
the contact surfaces shall be free from all contaminants, such as oil, dirt or paint. Burrs that would
prevent solid seating of the connecting parts shall be removed;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
uncoated surfaces shall be freed from all films of rust and other loose material. Care shall be taken not to
damage or smooth the roughened surface. Untreated areas around the perimeter of the tightened
connection shall be left untreated until any inspection of the connection has been completed.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Surface treatment that may be assumed to provide the minimum slip factor according to the specified class of
friction surface without test are given in Table 18.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Table 18 — Classifications that may be assumed for friction surfaces<<HEADING_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>These requirements apply also to packing plates provided to offset differences in thickness as specified in 8.1.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>8.5
Tightening of preloaded bolts<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>8.5.1
General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Unless otherwise specified the nominal minimum preloading force  F p,C  shall be taken as:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>F p,C  = 0,7  f ub A s   where  f ub  is the nominal ultimate strength of the bolt material and  A s  is the stress area of the
bolt<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>as defined in EN 1993-1-8 and specified in Table 19. This level of preload shall be used for all slip resistant
preloaded connections and for all other preloaded connections unless a lower level of preload is specified. In
the latter case, the bolt assemblies, the tightening method, the tightening parameters and the inspection
requirements shall also be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Preload may be used for slip resistance, for seismic connections, for fatigue resistance, for execution
purposes, or as a quality measure (e.g. for durability).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>Tightening method
k- classes<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Torque method
K2<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Combined method
K2 or K1<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>HRC tightening method
K0 with HRD nut only or K2<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Direct tension indicator (DTI) method
K2, K1 or K0<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>As an alternative, calibration to Annex H may be used, except for the torque method unless this is permitted in
the execution specification.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The as-delivered calibration is valid for tightening by rotation of the nut. If tightening is done by rotation of the
bolt head, calibration shall be done according to Annex H or by supplementary testing from the fastener
manufacturer otherwise in accordance with EN 14399-2.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Burrs, loose material and excessive thickness of paint that would prevent solid seating of the connecting parts
shall be removed before assembly.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Before commencement of preloading, the connected components shall be fitted together and the bolts in a
bolt group shall be tightened in accordance with 8.3 but the residual gap shall be limited to 2 mm with the
necessary corrective action on steel components.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Tightening shall be performed by rotation of the nut except where the access to the nut side of the assembly is
inadequate.   Special precautions, depending on the tightening method adopted, may have to be taken when
bolts are tightened by rotation of the bolt head.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Tightening shall be carried out progressively from the most rigid part of the joint to the least rigid part. To
achieve uniform preloading, more than one cycle of tightening may be necessary.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Torque wrenches used in all steps of the torque method shall be capable of an accuracy of ± 4 % according to
EN ISO 6789. Each wrench shall be checked for accuracy at least weekly, and in case of pneumatic
wrenches, every time the hose length is changed. For torque wrenches used in the first step of the combined
method these requirements are modified to ± 10 % for the accuracy and yearly for the periodicity.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Checking shall be carried out after any incident occurring during use (significant impact, fall, overloading etc.)
and affecting the wrench.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Other tightening methods (e.g. axial preloading by hydraulic devices or tensioning with ultrasonic control) shall
be calibrated in accordance with the recommendations from the equipment manufacturer.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>High strength bolts for preloading shall be used without alteration to the as-delivered lubrication unless DTI
method or the procedure in Annex H is adopted.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If a bolt assembly has been tightened to the minimum preload and is later un-tightened, it shall be removed
and the whole assembly shall be discarded.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Bolt assemblies used for achieving initial fit up should not generally need to be tightened to the minimum
preload or un-tightened, and would therefore still be usable in location in the final bolting up process.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
If the tightening process is delayed under uncontrolled exposure conditions the performance of the lubrication
may be altered and should be checked.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The potential loss of preloading force from its initial value due to several factors, e.g. relaxation, creep of
surface coatings (see Annex F.4 and Table 18), is considered in the tightening methods specified below. In
case of thick surface coatings, it shall be specified if measures shall be taken to offset possible subsequent
loss of preloading force.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>8.5.2
Torque reference values<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The torque reference values M r,i  to be used for a nominal minimum preloading force Fp,C are determined for
each type of bolt and nut combination used by one of the following options:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
values based on  k -class declared by the fastener manufacturer in accordance with the relevant parts of
EN 14399:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>1)  M r,2  =  k m   d   F p,C
with  k m  for  k -class K2.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>2)  M r,1  =  k m   d   F p,C
with  k m  for  k -class K1.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
values determined according to Annex H:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>1)  M r,test   = M m
with  M m  determined according to the procedure relevant to the tightening
method to be used.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>8.5.3
Torque method<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The bolts shall be tightened using a torque wrench offering a suitable operating range. Hand or power
operated wrenches may be used. Impact wrenches may be used for the first step of tightening for each bolt.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The tightening torque shall be applied continuously and smoothly.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Tightening by the torque method comprises at least the two following steps:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
a first tightening step: the wrench shall be set to a torque value of about 0,75  M r,i  with  M r,i  =  M r,2  or  M r,test .
This first step shall be completed for all bolts in one connection prior to commencement of the second
step;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
a second tightening step: the wrench shall be set to a torque value of 1,10  M r,i  with  M r,i  =  M r,2  or  M r,test.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
The use of the 1,10 coefficient with M r,2  is equivalent to (1 + 1,65 Vk) with Vk=0,06 for kclass K2.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>8.5.4
Combined method<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Tightening by the combined method comprises two steps:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) a first tightening step, using a torque wrench offering a suitable operating range. The wrench shall be set
to a torque value of about 0,75  M r,i  with  M r,i  =  M r,2  or  M r,1  or  M r,test . This first step shall be completed for all
bolts in one connection prior to commencement of the second step;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>When using  M r,1 , for simplification  M r,1  = 0,13 d Fp,C may be used unless otherwise specified<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) a second tightening step in which a specified part turn is applied to the turned part of the assembly. The
position of the nut relative to the bolt threads shall be marked after the first step, using a marking crayon
or marking paint, so that the final rotation of the nut relative to the thread in this second step can be easily
determined.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The second step shall be in accordance with the values given Table 21 unless otherwise specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>65<<HEADING_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>8.5.5
HRC method<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The HRC bolts shall be tightened using a specific shear wrench equipped with two co-axial sockets which
react by torque one against the other. The outer socket which engages the nut rotates clockwise. The inner
socket which engages the spline end of the bolt rotates anticlockwise.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 1 The shear wrench operates as follows:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>- during the tightening operation of an assembly, the socket in rotation is the one that finds the least resistance to it;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>- from the outset and right up to the last tightening stage, the outer socket on the nut rotates clockwise while the inner
socket holds the spline end without rotating, the result being that the bolt assembly is progressively tightened by the
increasing torque applied to the nut;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>- at the last tightening stage, i.e. when the torsional resistance plateau of the break-neck section is attained, the inner
socket rotates anticlockwise while the outer socket on nut provides the reaction without rotating;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>- the bolt assembly installation is complete when the spline end shears off at the break-neck section.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The specified preload requirement is controlled by the HRC bolt itself by means of the geometrical and torsion
mechanical characteristics together with the lubrication conditions. The equipment does not need calibration.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>In order to ensure that the preloads in fully installed bolts in connections meet the specified minimum preload
requirement, the bolt installation process generally comprises two tightening steps; both using the shear
wrench.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The first tightening step is achieved at the latest when the shear wrench outer socket stops turning. If
specified this first step is repeated as often as required. This first step shall be completed for all bolts in one
connection prior to commencement of the second step.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 2
Guidance of the equipment manufacturer may give additional information on how to identify if pretightening
has occurred, e.g. sound of shear wrench changing, or if other methods of pretightening are suitable.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The second tightening step is achieved when the spline end of the bolt shears off at the break-neck.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If the assembly conditions are such that it is not possible to use the shear wrench on the HRC bolt assembly,
e.g. for lack of space, tightening shall be carried out using the torque control method, see 8.5.3, with the aid of
the k-class K2 information or using a direct tension indicator, see 8.5.6.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>8.5.6
Direct tension indicator method<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This subclause applies to compressible washers, such as direct tension indicators in accordance with
prEN 14399-9, which indicate at least the required minimum preload has been achieved, by monitoring the<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>The direct tension indicators and their associated washers shall be assembled as specified in Annex J.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

initial deformation of the DTI protrusions begins. This first step shall be completed for all bolts in one
