<<PARAGRAPH>>The second step of tightening shall be as prEN 14399-9 and Annex J. The gaps measured on the indicating
washer may be averaged to establish the acceptability of the bolt assembly.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>8.6 Fit bolts<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Fit bolts may be used in preloaded or non-preloaded applications, and 8.1 to 8.5 apply as appropriate in
addition to the requirements below.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The length of the threaded portion of the shank of the fit bolt (including thread run out) included in the bearing
length should not exceed 1/3 of the thickness of the plate unless otherwise specified, see Figure 4.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<IMAGE_4>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Figure 4 — Threaded portion of the shank in the bearing length for fit bolts<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Fit bolts shall be installed without applying excessive force, and in such a way that its thread is not damaged.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>8.7 Hot riveting<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>8.7.1
Rivets<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Every rivet shall be of sufficient length to provide a head of uniform dimensions, a complete filling of the hole
and to avoid surface indentation by the riveting machine on the outer faces of the plies.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>8.7.2
Installation of rivets<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The connected components shall be drawn together such that they achieve firm contact and held together
during riveting.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Maximum eccentricity between common holes for a rivet in an assembly shall be no more than 1 mm. To meet
this requirement reaming is permitted. Following reaming it may be necessary to install a larger diameter of
rivet.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For multiple riveted connections, a temporary bolt shall be tightened in at least every fourth hole prior to
driving which shall start at the middle of the rivet group. Special measures shall be taken to hold components
of single riveted connections together (e.g. clamping).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>67<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_72>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If practicable, riveting shall be carried out using machines of the steady pressure type. After the upsetting is
complete, the driving pressure shall be maintained on the rivets for a short time sufficient for the head to be
black when the machine is disengaged.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Every rivet shall be heated uniformly throughout its length, without burning or excessive scaling. It shall be at
a consistent bright red heat from the head to point when inserted and shall be upset in its entire length when
hot, so as to fill the hole completely. Special care shall be taken in heating and driving long rivets.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Every rivet shall be freed from scale by striking the hot rivet on a hard surface after being heated and before
being inserted into the hole.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>A burned rivet shall not be used. A heated rivet not used immediately shall not be re-heated for use.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If a flush surface of countersunk rivets is specified protruding rivet metal shall be chipped or ground off.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>8.7.3
Acceptance criteria<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The rivet heads shall be centred. The head eccentricity relative to the shank axis shall not exceed
0,15  d 0  where  d 0  is the hole diameter.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The rivet heads shall be well formed and shall not show cracks or pits.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The rivets shall be in satisfactory contact with the assembled parts both at the outer surface of the plies and in
the hole. No movement or vibration shall be detected when the rivet head is lightly tapped with a hammer.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>A small well-formed and centred lip may be accepted if only a small number of rivets in the group are
concerned.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Outer faces of plies free of indentation by the riveting machine may be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If countersunk rivets are required the heads shall fill the countersink completely after riveting. If the
countersinking is not completely filled, the rivet shall be replaced.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Any rivet not meeting the acceptance criteria shall be removed and replaced by a new one.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>8.8 Fastening of thin gauge components<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>8.8.1
General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This clause applies to thin gauge components up to 4 mm thickness.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The performance of fasteners will depend on the site methodology that may be determined by procedure
testing. Procedure tests may be used to demonstrate that the required connections can be performed under
site conditions. The following aspects should be considered:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
ability to produce correct hole size for self-tapping screws and rivets;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
ability to correctly adjust power screwdrivers with the correct tightening torque/depth location;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c)
ability to drive a self-drilling screw perpendicular to the connected surface and set sealing washers to
correct compression within the limits recommended by the washer manufacturer;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d)
ability to select and use cartridge fired pins;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e)
ability to form an adequate structural connection and to recognize an inadequate one.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Fasteners shall be used in accordance with the product manufacturer's recommendations.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>68<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_73>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Use of special fasteners and fastening methods is dealt with in 8.9.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>8.8.2
Use of self-tapping and self-drilling screws<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The length and thread form of screws shall be selected to suit the specific application and the thickness of the
constituent product to be fastened. The effective thread length shall be such that the threaded portion
engages in the supporting component.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Screws for certain applications require an interrupted thread. If a sealing washer is used the thickness of the
washer should be taken into account in selecting the thread length.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The fasteners shall be located in the valley of the corrugation unless otherwise specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If screws are fastened in the crown of a roofing profile care shall be taken to avoid dents in the sheet at the
penetration point.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Power tools for fixing screws shall possess an adjustable depth and/or torque control that shall be set in
accordance with the equipment manufacturer's recommendations. If power screwdrivers are used, the drilling
and driving speeds (revolutions per minute) shall be in accordance with the fastener manufacturer's
recommendations.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If sealing washers are used, the screws shall be set to achieve the correct compression as indicated by Figure
5.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The depth gauge, of a power screwdriver, shall be adjusted to compress the elastomeric washer within the
limits set by the product manufacturer.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<IMAGE_5>>
[Image 5 contains text: OC) © XO]
<<HEADING level=3>>Figure 5 — Guide for compression of sealing washers<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Screws without sealing washers shall be set using an appropriate torque or depth control device to avoid
overtightening.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The torque control shall be set such that the threading torque is achieved without exceeding either the head-
shearing torque or the thread stripping torque.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>8.8.3
Use of blind rivets<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The choice of the length of the blind rivet shall be according to the total thickness to be fastened.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 1
The rivet length recommended by the product manufacturer generally takes account of a certain drawing
together of the plates to be fastened.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 2
Most manufacturers offer a range of manually and power operated setting tools to suit high or low volume
usage. These are often readily adaptable by changing only the nosepiece and/or setting jaws to set a range of blind rivet
types and sizes. Generally interchangeable heads are available for setting where tool access is limited such as inside
channels or cylindrical sections.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 3
Predetermined setting characteristics designed into the rivet body/mandrel relationship ensure consistent
joints.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>69<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_74>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Installation shall be performed according to the product manufacturer's recommendations.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>After installation work the ejected broken mandrel stems shall be collected and removed from exterior work
surfaces to prevent subsequent corrosion.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>8.8.4
Fastening sidelaps<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Connections securing panels to each other (sidelaps) and such items as flashing and accessories shall be
adequate to draw together overlapping sheets.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Sidelaps of profiled sheets of the exposed surface of a roof should be fastened according to the product
manufacturer's
recommendations.
The
minimum
diameter
of
these
fasteners
should
be
4,8 mm for self-tapping and self-drilling screws and 4,0 mm for blind rivets.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If the sheeting is intended to act as a stressed skin, the requirements for the side lap fasteners as structural
fasteners shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>8.9 Use of special fasteners and fastening methods<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Special fasteners shall be used and special fastening methods shall be performed in accordance with the
product manufacturer's recommendations, and the appropriate sections of 8.1 to 8.8. This also applies to bolts
connecting steelwork to other construction materials including chemically anchored foundation bolts.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 1
Examples of special fastening methods are specially tapped holes, threaded studs, adhesive bonding or
clinching using plates that are joined by local deformations.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Such methods shall be used only where specified. Any procedure tests required for use of special fasteners
and fastening methods in non-preloaded or preloaded applications shall be specified. Different tests from
those specified for bolts may be necessary. Procedure testing may be avoided if sufficient information on
previous testing is provided.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Specially tapped holes or threaded studs may be used as equivalent to the use of a bolting assembly in 5.6.3
provided that the materials, thread forms and thread tolerance comply with the respective product standard.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Requirements for use of hexagon injection bolts shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 2
Annex K provides information on the supply and use of hexagon injection bolts that may be invoked.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>8.10 Galling and seizure of stainless steels<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Galling may result from local adhesion and rupture of surfaces under load and in relative motion during
fastening. In some cases, weld bonding and seizure may result.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The following methods may be used to avoid galling problems:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
dissimilar standard grades of stainless steel may be used which vary in composition, work hardening rate
and
hardness
(e.g.
Grade
A2-C4,
A4-C4
or
A2-A4
bolt-nut
combination
from
EN ISO 3506-1 and EN ISO 3506-2);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
in severe cases, a proprietary high work-hardening stainless steel alloy may be used for one component
or hard surface coatings applied, e.g. nitriding or hard chromium plating;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c)
anti-galling agents such as PTFE dry film spray.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If dissimilar metals or coatings are used, it is necessary to ensure that the required corrosion resistance is
obtained.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>70<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_75>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
The greasing of bolts is beneficial but may result in contamination by dirt and can present problems for
storage.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9
Erection<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.1 General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This clause gives requirements for erection and other work undertaken on site including grouting of bases as
well as those relevant to the suitability of the site for safe erection and for accurately prepared supports.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Work carried out on site which includes preparation, welding, mechanical fastening and surface treatment
shall comply with the Clauses 6, 7, 8 and 10 respectively.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Inspection and acceptance of the structure shall be performed in accordance with the requirements specified
in Clause 12.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.2 Site conditions<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Erection shall not commence until the site for the construction works complies with the technical requirements
with respect to the safety of the works, which shall consider such of the following items as are relevant:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) provision and maintenance of hard standing for cranes and access equipment;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) access routes to the site and within the site;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) soil conditions affecting the safe operation of plant;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) possible settlement of erection supports for the structure;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) details of underground services, overhead cables or site obstructions;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f)
limitations on dimensions or weights of components that can be delivered onto the site;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>g) special environmental and climatic conditions on and around the site;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>h) particulars of adjacent structures affecting or affected by the works.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Access routes to the site and within the site should be given on a site plan showing dimensions and level of
access routes, level of the prepared working area for site traffic and plant, and areas available for storage.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If the works are inter-linked with other trades, technical requirements with respect to the safety of the works
shall be checked for consistency with those for other parts of the construction works. This check shall consider
such of the following items as are relevant:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>i)
prearranged procedures for co-operation with other contractors;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>j)
availability of site services;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>k) maximum construction and storage loads permitted on the steelwork;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>l)
control of concrete placement during composite construction.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
EN 1991-1-6 provides rules for determining construction and storage loads including concrete.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>71<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_76>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.3 Erection method<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.3.1
Design basis for the erection method<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If the structural stability in the part-erected condition is not evident, a safe method of erection on which the
design was based shall be provided. This design basis method of erection shall consider the following items:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) positions and types of site connections;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) maximum piece size, weight and location;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) sequence of erection;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) stability concept for the part-erected structure including any requirements for temporary bracing or
propping;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) propping or other measures for the execution of phased concreting of composite structures;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f)
conditions for removal of temporary bracing or propping, or any requirement for distressing or stressing
the structure;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>g) features which would create a safety hazard during construction;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>h) timing and method for adjustment of foundation connections or bearings and for grouting;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>i)
camber and presets required in relation of those provided at manufacturing stage;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>j)
use of profiled steel sheeting to ensure stability;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>k) use of profiled steel sheeting to provide lateral restraint;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>l)
transportation of units, including attachments for lifting, turning or pulling;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>m) positions and conditions for supporting and jacking;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>n) stability concept for the bearings;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>o) deformations of the partly erected structure;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>p) expected settlements of the supports;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>q) particular positions and loads from cranes, stored components, counter weight etc. for the various
construction phases;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>r)
instructions for the delivery, storage, lifting, building in and pre-tensioning of stayed cables;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>s) details of all temporary works and attachments to permanent works with instructions as to their removal.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.3.2
Constructor's erection method<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>A method statement describing the constructor's erection method shall be prepared and it shall be checked in
accordance with design rules, notably against resistance of the partly erected structure to erection loads and
other loading.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The erection method statement may deviate from the design basis method of erection, provided that it is a
safe alternative.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>72<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_77>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Amendments to the erection method statement, including those necessitated by site conditions, shall be
checked and reviewed in accordance with the above requirement.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The erection method statement shall describe procedures to be used to safely erect the steelwork and shall
take into account the technical requirements regarding the safety of the works.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The procedures should link to specific work instructions.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The erection method statement shall address all relevant items in 9.3.1, and shall consider in addition such of
the following items as are relevant:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
experience from any trial erection undertaken in accordance with 9.6.4;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
restraints necessary to ensure stability prior to welding and to control local movement of the joint;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c)
lifting devices necessary;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d)
necessity to mark weights and/or centres of gravity on large or irregularly shaped pieces;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e)
relationship between the weights to be lifted and the radius of operation where cranes are to be used;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f)
identification of sway or overturning forces, particularly those due to the predicted wind conditions on site
during erection, and the exact methods of maintaining adequate sway and overturning resistance;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>g)
methods of coping with safety hazards;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>h)
provision of safe working positions and safe means of access to them.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>In addition, the following apply for composite steel and concrete structures:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>i)
sequence of fixing of profiled steel sheeting for composite slabs shall be planned to ensure that sheets
are adequately supported by supporting beams before fixing, and are securely fixed before they are used
to gain access to subsequent working positions;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>j)
profiled steel sheets should not be used to gain access for welding of shear connectors unless the
sheets are secured already by fasteners that comply with i);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>k)
sequence of placing and method of securing and sealing permanent formwork to ensure that formwork is
secure before being used to gain access for subsequent construction operations and supporting slab
reinforcement and deck concrete.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Factors associated with the execution of the concrete works should be considered as relevant, such as
sequence of placing concrete, pre-stressing, and temperature difference between steel and freshly placed
concrete, jacking and supports.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.4 Survey<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.4.1
Reference system<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Site measurements for the works shall be related to the system established for the setting out and
measurement of the construction works in accordance with ISO 4463-1.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>A documented survey of a secondary net shall be provided and used as the reference system for setting out
the steelwork and establishing the deviations of supports. The coordinates of the secondary net given in this
survey shall be accepted as true provided that they comply with the acceptance criteria specified in
ISO 4463-1.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The reference temperature for setting out and measuring the steelwork shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>73<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_78>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.4.2
Position points<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The position points which mark the intended position for the erection of individual components shall be in
accordance with ISO 4463-1.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.5 Supports, anchors and bearings<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.5.1
Inspection of supports<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The condition and location of the supports shall be checked using appropriate visual and measurement means
before the commencement of erection.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If supports are unsuited to erection, they shall be corrected prior to the commencement of erection.
Nonconformities shall be documented.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.5.2
Setting out and suitability of supports<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>All foundations, foundation bolts and other supports for the steelwork shall be suitably prepared to receive the
steel
structure.
Installation
of
structural
bearings
shall
comply
with
the
requirements
of
EN 1337-11.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Erection shall not commence until the location and levels of the supports, anchors or bearings comply with the
acceptance criteria in 11.2, or an appropriate amendment to the specified requirements has been issued.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The compliance survey used to check the positions of the supports shall be documented.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If foundation bolts are to be pre-stressed, arrangement shall be made that the upper 100 mm, as a minimum,
of the bolt has no adhesion to the concrete.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Foundation bolts intended to move in sleeves should be provided with sleeves three times the diameter of the
bolt with a minimum of 75 mm.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.5.3
Maintaining suitability of supports<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Whilst erection is proceeding, the supports for the steelwork shall be maintained in an equivalent condition to
their condition at the commencement of erection.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 1
Areas of supports that require protection against rust staining should be identified and appropriate protection
provided.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Compensation for settlement of supports is acceptable, unless otherwise specified. This shall be done by
grouting or packing between steelwork and support.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 2
The compensation will generally be placed beneath the bearing.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.5.4
Temporary supports<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Shims and other supporting devices used as temporary supports under base plates shall present a flat surface
to the steel and be of adequate size, strength and rigidity to avoid local crushing of the substructure concrete
or masonery.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If packings are subsequently to be grouted, they shall be placed so that the grout totally encloses them with a
minimum cover of 25 mm unless otherwise specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For bridges, packings shall not be left in position, unless otherwise specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>74<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_79>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If packings are left in position after grouting they shall be made from materials with the same durability as the
structure.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If adjustment to the position of the base is achieved using levelling nuts on the foundation bolts under the
base plate these may be left in position unless otherwise specified. The nuts shall be selected to ensure that
they are suitable to maintain the stability of the part-erected structure but not to jeopardise the performance of
the foundation bolt in service.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
As well as shims and blocks, half-nuts or plastic nuts are often used as levelling nuts.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.5.5
Grouting and sealing<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If spaces under base plates are to be grouted, fresh material shall be used in accordance with 5.8.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Grouting material shall be used as follows:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) the material shall be mixed and used in accordance with product manufacturer's recommendations
notably regarding its consistency when used. Material shall not be mixed or used below 0 °C unless the
manufacturer's recommendations permit it;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) the material shall be poured under a suitable head so that the space is completely filled;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) tamping and ramming against properly fixed supports shall be used if specified and/or recommended by
the grout manufacturer;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) vent holes shall be provided as necessary.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Immediately before grouting, the space under the steel base plate shall be free from liquids, ice, debris and
contaminants.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Pocket bases containing columns shall be filled with dense concrete having a characteristic compressive
strength not less than that of the surrounding concrete.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>In pocket bases, the embedded length of the column shall be initially surrounded with concrete to a sufficient
length to provide stability in the temporary state and then remain undisturbed for a period sufficient to gain at
least half of its characteristic compressive strength, before removal of any temporary props and wedges.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If treatment of steelwork, bearings and concrete surfaces is required before grouting, it shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Care shall be taken that the external profile of grouting allows water to be drained away from structural steel
components.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If there is a danger of water or corrosive liquid becoming entrapped during service, the grout around base
plates shall not be surcharged such that it rises above the lowest surface of the base plate and the geometry
of the concrete grout shall form an angle from the base plate according to Figure 6.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If no grouting is needed, and the edges of the base plate are to be sealed, the method shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>75<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>Figure 6 — Grouting under base plate<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The concrete and the grouting shall be carried out according to 5.8 and prEN 13670.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.5.6
Anchoring<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Anchoring devices in concrete parts of the structure or adjacent structures shall be set in accordance with
their specification.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Suitable measures shall be taken to avoid damage to concrete in order to achieve the necessary anchoring
resistance.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
This applies notably to expansion anchors, for which a minimum distance from the facing is necessary in order
to avoid concrete bursting.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.6 Erection and work at site<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.6.1
Erection drawings<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Erection drawings or equivalent instructions shall be provided and form a part of the erection method
statement.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Drawings shall be prepared showing plans and elevations and at such a scale that the erection marks for all
components can be shown on them.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Drawings shall show grid locations, bearing positions and assembly of components together with
requirements for tolerances.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Foundation plans shall show the base location and orientation of the steelwork, any other components in
direct contact with the foundations, their base location and level, the intended bearing level and the datum
level. Foundations shall include column base support and other structural supports.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Elevations shall show required levels for floors and/or structure.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Drawings shall show necessary details for fixing of steel or bolts to the foundations, the method of adjustment
by packing and wedging and grout requirements as well as fixing of steelwork and bearings to their supports.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Drawings shall show details and arrangements of any steelwork or other temporary works necessary for
erection purposes to ensure the stability of the construction or the safety of personnel.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Drawings shall state the weight of all components or assemblies over 5 tonnes and the centre of gravity of all
large irregular pieces.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For thin gauge sheeting installation drawings are necessary and shall as a minimum and as relevant specify:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>76<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_81>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) type, thickness, material, length and designation of sheets;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) type of fasteners and order (sequence) of fastenings including special installation notes for the type of
fasteners (e.g. drilled hole diameter and minimum torque);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) structural system for the sheeting;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) seam and sidelap joints with specification of the type of fasteners and washers and sequence;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) requirements for on-site manufacturing;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f)
positions of all site connections not using pre-drilled holes;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>g) type and details pertaining to the sub-assembly of the sheets, such as material, axial intervals, formation
of supports, slope and details of eaves and verges;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>h) expansion joints;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>i)
openings and necessary framing (e.g. lighting domes, smoke and heat ventilation installations and roof
drainage);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>j)
mountings and attachments (e.g. for piping, cable conduits and sub-ceilings);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>k) limitations of walkability during installation and requirements for load distributing devices.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.6.2
Marking<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Components that are individually assembled or erected at the site shall be allocated an erection mark.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>A component shall be marked with its erected orientation if this is not clear from its shape.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Marks should be placed, if possible, in positions where they will be visible in storage and after erection.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Marking methods shall comply with 6.2.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.6.3
Handling and storage on site<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Handling and storage on site shall comply with the requirements of 6.3 and those given below.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Components shall be handled and stacked in such a way that the likelihood of damage is minimized.
Particular attention shall be paid to slinging methods to avoid damage to the steelwork and protective
treatment.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Steelwork damaged during off-loading, transportation, storage or erection shall be restored to conformity.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The procedure for restoration shall be defined before undertaking the repair. For EXC2, EXC 3 and EXC 4 the
procedure shall also be documented.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Fasteners stored on site shall be kept in dry conditions prior to use and shall be suitably packed and
identifiable.The fasteners shall be handled and used in accordance with the manufacturer's recommendations.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>All small plates and other fittings shall be suitably packed and identified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.6.4
Trial erection<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Any site trial erection shall be performed in accordance with the requirements of 6.10.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Trial erection should be considered:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>77<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_82>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) to confirm fit between components;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) to prove methodology if the erection sequence to maintain stability during erection needs evaluating in
advance;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) to prove duration of operations if site conditions are restricted by limited possession time.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.6.5
Erection methods<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.6.5.1
General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The erection of the steelwork shall be carried out in conformity with the erection method statement and in such
a way as to ensure stability at all times.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Foundation bolts shall not be used to secure unguyed columns against overturning unless they have been
checked for this mode of use.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Throughout the erection of the structure, the steelwork shall be made safe against temporary erection loads,
including those due to erection equipment or its operation and against the effects of wind loads on the
unfinished structure.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For buildings, at least one third of the permanent bolts in each connection should be installed before that
connection can be considered to contribute to stability of the part completed structure.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.6.5.2
Temporary works<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>All temporary bracing and temporary restraints shall be left in position until erection is sufficiently advanced to
allow its safe removal.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If it is required that bracings in tall buildings are to be de-stressed as erection progresses, to release the
forces induced in them by vertical loads, this shall be carried out progressively one panel at a time. During
such de-stressing sufficient alternative bracing shall be in place to ensure stability.  If necessary, additional
bracing shall be added temporarily for this purpose.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>All connections for temporary components provided for erection purposes shall be made in accordance with
the requirements of this European Standard and in such a way that they do not weaken the permanent
structure or impair its serviceability.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If backing bars and draw cleats are used to support the structure during welding, it shall be ensured that they
are sufficiently strong and that their retaining welds are appropriate for the erection load conditions.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If the erection procedure involves rolling or otherwise moving the structure, or part of the structure, into its final
position after assembly, provision shall be made for controlled braking of the moving mass. Provision for
reversing the direction of movement may need to be considered.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>All temporary anchoring devices shall be made secure against unintentional release.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Only jacks that can be locked in any position under load shall be used unless other safety provisions are
made.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.6.5.3
Fit-up and alignment<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Care shall be taken that no part of the structure is permanently distorted or over-stressed by stacking of
steelwork components or by erection loads during the erection process.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Each part of the structure shall be aligned as soon as practicable after it has been erected and final assembly
completed as soon as possible thereafter.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>78<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_83>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Permanent connections shall not be made between components until sufficient of the structure has been
aligned, levelled, plumbed and temporarily connected to ensure that components will not be displaced during
subsequent erection or alignment of the remainder of the structure.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Alignment of the structure and lack of fit in connections may be adjusted by the use of shims. Shims shall be
secured where they are in danger of coming loose. For EXC3 and EXC4 securing of shims by welding is
subjected to the requirements of Clause 7.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Shims shall be made of flat steel unless otherwise specified. Shims shall have similar durability to that of the
structure. For stainless steel structures they shall be made of stainless steel and have a minimum thickness of
2 mm if used externally.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If shims are used to align structures composed of coated material, the shims shall be protected in a similar
manner to provide the specified durability unless the shims are required to meet a specified friction
classification.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Residual gaps for non-preloaded bolts and preloaded bolts before preloading shall be in accordance with 8.3
and 8.5.1 respectively.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If lack-of-fit between erected components cannot be corrected by the use of shims, components of the
structure shall be locally modified in accordance with the methods specified in this European Standard. The
modifications shall not compromise the performance of the structure in the temporary or permanent state. This
work may be executed on site. Care shall be taken with structures built of welded latticed components and
space structures to ensure that they are not subjected to excessive forces in an attempt to force a fit against
their inherent rigidity.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Unless otherwise prohibited, drifts may be used to align connections. Elongation of holes for bolts used for
transmission of loads shall not be more than the values given in 6.9.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>In case of misalignment of holes for bolts, the method of correction shall be checked for consistency with the
requirements of Clause 12.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Realigned holes may be proven to comply with the oversize or slotted hole requirements specified in 8.1
provided the load path has been checked.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Correction of misalignment by reaming or using a hollow milling cutter is preferred, but if the use of other
cutting methods is unavoidable the internal finish of all holes formed by these other methods shall be
specifically checked for consistency with the requirements of Clause 6.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Completed site connections shall be checked in accordance with 12.5.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>10 Surface treatment<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>10.1 General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This clause specifies requirements for making steel surfaces with imperfections, including welded and
fabricated surfaces, suitable for the application of paints and related products. The requirements to take
account of the particular coating system to be applied shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This clause does not deal with the detailed requirements for corrosion protection systems, which are specified
in the following references that shall be applied as relevant:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) surfaces to be painted: EN ISO 12944 series and Annex F;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) surfaces to be metal coated by thermal spraying: EN 14616, EN 15311, EN ISO 14713 and
Annex F;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>79<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_84>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) surfaces to be metal coated by galvanizing: EN ISO 1461, EN ISO 14713 and Annex F.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For mechanical resistance and stability reasons there is no need for corrosion protection if the structure is to
be used for a short service lifetime, or in an environment with negligible corrosivity (e.g. category C1 or
painting for aesthetic purposes only), or has been dimensioned to allow for corrosion.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 1
A year may be considered as a short service lifetime.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If painting is specified for aesthetic reasons Table 22 together with Annex F are applicable.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If both a fire protection and corrosion protection systems are specified, they shall be proven to be compatible.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 2
Fire protection is not generally considered to be a part of the corrosion protection.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>10.2 Preparation of steel substrates<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>These requirements do not apply to stainless steels. If there are requirements for surface cleanliness of
stainless steels, they shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>All surfaces to which paints and related products are to be applied shall be prepared to meet the criteria of
EN ISO 8501. The preparation grade according to EN ISO 8501-3 shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If the expected life of the corrosion protection and corrosivity category are specified, the preparation grade
shall be in accordance with Table 22.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>80<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>Thermally cut surfaces, edges and welds shall be suitably smooth and able to achieve the specified
roughness after subsequent surface preparation (see Annex F).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Thermally cut surfaces are sometimes too hard for the abrasive material to achieve the suitable surface
roughness. The procedure test specified in 6.4.4 may be used to establish surface hardness and determine whether
grinding is necessary.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>10.3 Weather resistant steels<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If necessary, procedures to ensure that the surface of uncoated weather resistant steels is acceptable visually
after weathering shall be specified together with procedures to prevent contamination (e.g. from oil, grease,
paint, concrete or asphalt).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
As an example, exposed areas may need to be blast cleaned to ensure uniform weathering.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The treatment necessary for surfaces of non-weather resistant steels if these are in contact with uncoated
weather resistant steels shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>10.4 Galvanic coupling<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Unintended contact between different metallic constituent products, e.g. stainless steels to aluminium or
structural steel shall be avoided. If stainless steel is to be welded to structural steel, corrosion protection for
the steel structure shall continue from the weld on to the stainless steel by 20 mm as a minimum. See also
6.3, 6.9 and 7.7.3.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>10.5 Galvanizing<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If pickling is to be used prior to galvanizing, all weld gaps should be sealed prior to pickling to prevent the
ingress of acid, unless this conflicts with considerations set out in 10.6 below.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If the fabricated component contains enclosed spaces, vent and drain holes shall be provided. The enclosed
space shall generally be galvanized internally and if not it shall be specified whether these enclosed spaces
shall be sealed after galvanizing and, if so, with what.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<PAGE_86>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>10.6 Sealing of spaces<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If enclosed spaces are to be sealed by welding or provided with internal protective treatment, the internal
treatment system shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If spaces are to be fully enclosed by welds, it shall be specified if weld imperfections permitted under the
welding specification require sealing by application of suitable filler material to prevent the ingress of moisture.
If welds are for sealing purposes only, those welds shall be visually inspected. If required, further inspection
shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Attention is drawn that cracks in welds, which are not detectable by visual inspection, can allow water to
penetrate the sealed space.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If closed sections are to be galvanized, they shall not be sealed before galvanizing. In the case of overlapping
surfaces with continuous welds, adequate venting shall be provided, unless the area of overlap is so small
that the risk of explosive egress of entrapped gases during the galvanizing operation is assessed as not
significant.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If mechanical fasteners penetrate the wall of sealed enclosed spaces, the method to be used for sealing the
interface shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>10.7 Surfaces in contact with concrete<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Surfaces that are to be in contact with concrete including the undersides of baseplates shall be coated with
the protective treatment applied to the steelwork, excluding any cosmetic finishing coat, for a minimum of the
first 50 mm of the embedded length unless otherwise specified and the remaining surfaces need not be
coated unless specified. If uncoated, such surfaces shall be blast cleaned or wire-brushed to remove loose
mill scale and cleaned to remove dust, oil and grease. Immediately before concreting, any loose rust, dust and
other loose debris shall be removed by cleaning.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>10.8 Inaccessible surfaces<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Areas and surfaces that are difficult to access after assembly should be treated before assembly.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>In slip resistant connections, faying surfaces shall meet the requirements necessary to develop the friction for
the specified surface treatment (see 8.4). Other connections shall not be made with excess paint on the faying
surfaces. As a maximum, faying surfaces and surfaces beneath washers shall be treated with a primer and
undercoat unless specified otherwise (see F.4).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Unless specified otherwise, bolted connections including the perimeter around such connections shall be
treated with the full corrosion protection system specified for the remainder of the steelwork.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>10.9 Repairs after cutting or welding<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>It shall be specified if repair, or additional protective treatment, is required to cut edges and adjacent surfaces
after cutting.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If precoated constituent products are to be welded, the methods and extent of repair necessary to the coating
shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If galvanizing to surfaces has been removed or damaged by welding, the surfaces shall be cleaned, prepared
and treated with a zinc rich primer and paint system offering a similar level of corrosion protection as the
galvanizing for the given corrosivity category (see EN ISO 1461 for additional guidance).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>82<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_87>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>10.10 Cleaning after erection<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>10.10.1 Cleaning of thin gauge components<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The structure shall be cleaned daily from stems of blind rivets, drill-shavings etc., to prevent damage by
corrosion.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>10.10.2 Cleaning of stainless steels components<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Cleaning procedures shall be appropriate for the grade of constituent product, surface finish, function of the
component and corrosion risk. The method, level and extent of cleaning shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Strong acid solutions sometimes used to clean the masonry and tiling of buildings shall not be permitted to
come into contact with structural steel, including stainless steel. If such contamination does happen, acid
solutions shall be washed off immediately with large amounts of clean water.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>11 Geometrical tolerances<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>11.1 Tolerance types<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This clause defines the types of geometrical deviations and gives quantitative values for two types of
permitted deviations:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) those applicable for a range of criteria that are essential for the mechanical resistance and stability of the
completed structure, called essential tolerances;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) those required to fulfil other criteria such as fit-up and appearance, called functional tolerances.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Essential tolerances and functional tolerances are both normative.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
For structural steel components, prEN 1090-1 refers to the essential tolerances.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The permitted deviations given do not include elastic deformations induced by the self-weight of the
components.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>In addition, special tolerances may be specified either for geometrical deviations already defined with
quantitative values or for other types of geometrical deviations. If special tolerances are required the following
information shall be given as appropriate:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  amended values for functional tolerances already defined;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  defined parameters and permitted values for the geometrical deviations to be controlled;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  whether these special tolerances apply to all relevant components or only to particular components that
are specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>In each case, the requirements are for final acceptance testing. If fabricated components are to form parts of a
structure that is to be erected on site, the tolerances specified for the final checking of the erected structure
shall be met in addition to those for the fabricated components.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>83<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_88>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>11.2 Essential tolerances<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>11.2.1 General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Essential tolerances shall be in accordance with D.1. The values specified are permitted deviations. If the
actual deviation exceeds the permitted value, the measured value shall be dealt with as a nonconformity
according to Clause 12.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>In some cases there is a possibility that the uncorrected deviation of an essential tolerance can be justified in
accordance with the structural design when the excess deviation is included explicitly in a recalculation. If not,
the nonconformity shall be corrected.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>11.2.2 Manufacturing tolerances<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>11.2.2.1
Rolled sections<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Hot rolled, hot finished or cold formed structural products shall conform to the permitted deviations specified
by the relevant product standard. These permitted deviations continue to apply to components manufactured
from such products, unless superseded by more stringent criteria specified in D.1.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>11.2.2.2
Welded sections<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Welded components manufactured from plates shall conform to the permitted deviations in
Table D.1.1 and Tables D.1.3 to D.1.6.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>11.2.2.3
Cold formed sections<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Components cold formed by pressing shall conform to the permitted deviations in Table D.1.2. For
components fabricated from rolled cold formed sections, see 11.2.2.1.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
As examples, cross-sectional tolerances for welded sections manufactured from split rolled sections would be
in accordance with the relevant product standard except for overall depth and web geometry which should be in
accordance with Table D.1.1; and cross sectional tolerances from EN 10162 apply to cold rolled sections whereas Table
D.1.2 applies to sections formed by pressing.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>11.2.2.4
Stiffened plating<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Stiffened plating shall conform to the permitted deviations in Table D.1.6.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>11.2.2.5
Profiled sheets<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Profiled sheets used as structural components shall conform to the permitted deviations specified in
EN 508-1 and EN 508-3 plus those in Table D.1.7.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>11.2.2.6
Shells<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Shell structures shall conform to the permitted deviations in Table D.1.9, in which the choice of the appropriate
class shall be based on EN 1993-1-6.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>11.2.3 Erection tolerances<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>11.2.3.1
Reference system<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Deviations of erected components shall be measured relative to their position points (see ISO 4463). If a
position point is not established, deviations shall be measured relative to the secondary system.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>84<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_89>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>11.2.3.2
Foundation bolts and other supports<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The position of the centre points of a group of foundation bolts or other support shall not deviate by more than
± 6 mm from its specified position relative to the secondary system.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>A best-fit position should be chosen to assess a group of adjustable foundation bolts.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>11.2.3.3
Column bases<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Holes in baseplates and other plates used for fixing to supports should be dimensioned to allow clearances to
match the permitted deviations for the supports to those for the steelwork. This may require the use of large
washers between the nuts on the holding down bolts and the top of the baseplate.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>11.2.3.4
Columns<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The deviations of erected columns shall conform to the permitted deviations in Tables D.1.10 to D.1.11.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For groups of adjacent columns (other than those in portal frames or supporting a crane gantry) carrying
similar vertical loads, the permitted deviations shall be as follows:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) the arithmetic average deviation in plan for the inclination of six tied adjacent columns shall conform to the
permitted deviations in Tables D.1.10 to D.1.11;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) the permitted deviations for the inclination of an individual column within this group, between adjacent
storey levels may then be relaxed to  ∆  = ±  h /100.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>11.2.3.5
Full contact bearing<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Where full contact bearing is specified, the fit-up between surfaces of erected components shall be in
accordance with Table D.1.12 after alignment.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For bolted splices shims may be used where the gap exceeds the specified limits after initial bolting-up, to
reduce the gaps to within the permitted deviation, unless otherwise specified in the execution specification.
The shims may be made of flat mild steel. No more than three shims shall be used at any point. If necessary,
the shims may be held in place by means of either fillet welds or a partial penetration butt weld extending over
the shims, as shown in Figure 7.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>11.3 Functional tolerances<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>11.3.1 General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Functional tolerances in terms of accepted geometrical deviations shall be in accordance with one of the
following two options:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) the tabulated values described in 11.3.2, or<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) the alternative criteria defined in 11.3.3.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If no option is specified the tabulated values shall apply.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>11.3.2 Tabulated values<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Tabulated values for functional tolerances are given in D.2. Generally values for two classes are shown. The
choice of tolerance class may be applied to individual components or selected parts of an erected structure.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
How D.2 can be applied would be to invoke tolerance class 2 for part of a structure to which a glazed facade
was to be fitted, in order to reduce the amount of clearance and adjustability required at the interface.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If D.2 is used, and the choice of class is not specified, tolerance class 1 applies.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>In applying Table D.2.19, the protruding length of a vertical foundation bolt (in its best-fit position if adjustable)
should be vertical to within 1 mm in 20 mm. A similar requirement would apply to the line of bolts set
horizontally or at other angles.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>11.3.3 Alternative criteria<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If specified the following alternative criteria may be applied:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
for welded structures, the following classes according to EN ISO 13920 apply:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>1) class C for length and angular dimensions;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>2) class G for straightness, flatness and parallelism;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
for non-welded components the same criteria as in (a);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>86<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_91>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c)
in other cases, for a dimension  d , a permitted deviation ±  ∆  equal to the greater of  d  /500 or 5 mm is
allowed.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12 Inspection, testing and correction<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.1 General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This clause specifies the requirements for inspection and testing with respect to the quality requirements
included in quality documentation (see 4.2.1) or quality plan (see 4.2.2) as relevant.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Inspection, testing and corrections shall be undertaken on the works against the specification and within the
quality requirements set out in this European Standard.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>All inspection and testing shall be undertaken to a predetermined plan with documented procedures. Specific
inspection testing and associated corrections shall be documented.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.2 Constituent products and components<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.2.1 Constituent products<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Documents supplied with constituent products in accordance with the requirements of Clause 5 shall be
checked to verify that the information on the products supplied matches those ordered.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 1
These documents include inspection certificates, test reports, declaration of compliance as relevant for plates,
sections, hollow sections, welding consumables, mechanical fasteners, studs etc.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 2
This documentation check is intended to obviate the need for testing products generally.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The inspection of the surface of product for defects revealed during surface preparation shall be included in
the inspection and test plans.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If surface defects in steel products revealed during surface preparation are repaired using methods that are in
accordance with this European Standard, the repaired product may be used provided that it complies with the
nominal properties specified for the original product.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>There are no requirements for specific testing of products unless otherwise specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.2.2 Components<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Documents supplied with components shall be checked to verify that the information on the components
supplied matches those ordered.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
This applies to all delivered and part-fabricated products received into a constructor's works for further
processing (e.g. welded  I -sections for incorporation into plate girders), and to products received on site for erection by the
constructor if these are not manufactured by the constructor.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.2.3 Non conforming products<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If the documentation supplied does not include a declaration from the supplier that the products conform to the
specifications, they shall be treated as non conforming products until it can be demonstrated that they meet
the requirements of the inspection and test plan.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If products are first designated as nonconforming and are subsequently proved to be in conformity by test or
retest, the testing shall be recorded.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>87<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_92>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.3 Manufacturing: geometrical dimensions of manufactured components<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The inspection plan shall consider the requirements and the checks necessary on prepared constituent steel
products and manufactured components.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Dimensional measurements of components shall always be taken. Methods and instruments used shall be
selected, as appropriate, from those listed in ISO 7976-1 and ISO 7976-2. Accuracy shall be assessed in
accordance with the relevant part of ISO 17123.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The location and frequency of measurements shall be specified in the inspection plan.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The acceptance criteria shall be in accordance with 11.2. The deviations shall be measured with respect to
any specified camber or preset.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If acceptance inspection results in the identification of nonconformity, the action on such nonconformity shall
be as follows:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) if practicable, the nonconformity shall be corrected using methods that are in accordance with this
European Standard and checked again;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) if correction is not practicable, modifications to the steel structure may be made to compensate for the
nonconformity provided that this is in accordance with a procedure for handling nonconformities.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Damage resulting in local dents in the surface of hollow sections shall be assessed. The method shown in
Figure 8 may be used.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<IMAGE_8>>
[Image 8 contains text: —e S|

<<PARAGRAPH>>Characteristic cross-sectional dimension of section is d
Straight edge of length L  ≥  2d Gap  ∆   ≤  the larger of  d /100 or 2 mm<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Figure 8 — Method of assessment for surface profile and permitted deviation of a dented component<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If the gap exceeds the permitted deviation, repairs may be executed by means of fully welding on local cover
plates of the same thickness as the original constituent product unless otherwise specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Such repairs are not uncommon, because many hollow sections have relatively thin walls.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This procedure should be used in preference to any hot-shaping procedure in accordance with 6.5.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If trial assembly to 6.10 is used the inspection requirements shall be included in the inspection plan.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.4 Welding<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.4.1 Inspection before and during welding<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Inspection before and during welding shall be included in the inspection plan according to the requirements
given in the relevant part of EN ISO 3834.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>88<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_93>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Non destructive testing (NDT) methods shall be selected in accordance with EN 12062 by personnel qualified
according to Level 3 as defined in EN 473. Generally ultrasonic testing or radiographic testing applies to butt
welds and penetrant testing or magnetic particle inspection applies to fillet welds.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NDT, with the exception of visual inspection, shall be performed by personnel qualified according to Level 2 as
defined in EN 473.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If the inspection plan requires a check of the fit-up before the welding of hollow sections prepared for branch
welding, the following locations shall be given particular attention:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  for circular sections: the mid-toe, mid-heel and two mid-flank positions;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  for square or rectangular sections: the four corner positions.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.4.2 Inspection after welding<<HEADING_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>The supplementary NDT of a weld shall generally not be completed until after the minimum hold time after
welding shown in Table 23.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>12.4.2.2

<<PARAGRAPH>>All welds shall be visually inspected throughout their entire length. If surface imperfections are detected,
surface testing by penetrant testing or magnetic particle inspection shall be carried out on the inspected weld.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

welds the extent of supplementary NDT is as specified below.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The extent of NDT covers both testing of surface or internal imperfections if applicable.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>Once it has been established that production welding according to a WPS meets the quality requirements, the
required extent of supplementary NDT shall be in accordance with Table 24 with further joints welded
according to the same WPS treated as a single continuing inspection lot. The percentages apply to the extent
of supplementary NDT treated as the cumulative amount within each inspection lot.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The joints for inspection according to Table 24 shall be selected on the basis of Annex C of
EN 12062:1997, with a minimum total length for an inspection lot  x  of 900 mm, ensuring that sampling covers
the following variables as widely as possible: the joint type, the constituent product grade, the welding
equipment and the work of the welders.   The execution specification may identify specific joints for inspection
together with the extent and method of testing.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If inspection discovers weld defects within an inspection length in excess of the requirements specified in the
acceptance criteria, inspection shall be undertaken over two inspection lengths, one on each side of the length
including the defect. If inspection on one or other side gives non conforming results, investigation shall be
carried out in order to find the reason.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 2
The purpose of the inspection in Table 24 is to establish that ongoing production is producing conforming
welds.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>12.4.2.3
Visual inspection of welds<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The visual inspection shall be performed after completion of welding in an area and before any other NDT
inspection is carried out.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Visual inspection shall include:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
the presence and location of all welds;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
inspection of the welds in accordance with EN 970;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c)
stray arcs and areas of weld spatter.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The inspection of the shape and surface of welds of welded branch joints using hollow sections shall pay
careful attention to the following locations:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) for circular sections: the mid-toe, mid-heel and two mid-flank positions;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) for square or rectangular sections: the four corner positions.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
