<<HEADING level=3>>12.4.2.4
Additional NDT methods<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The following NDT methods shall be carried out in accordance with the general principles given in
EN 12062 and with the requirements of the standard particular to each method:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
penetrant testing (PT) according to EN 571-1;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
magnetic particle inspection (MT) according to EN 1290;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c)
ultrasonic testing (UT) according to EN 1714, EN 1713;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d)
radiographic testing (RT) according to EN 1435.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The field of application of NDT methods is specified in their relevant standards.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.4.2.5
Correction of welds<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For EXC2, EXC3 and EXC4, repairs by welding shall be carried out in accordance with qualified welding
procedures.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Corrected welds shall be checked and shall meet the requirements of the original welds.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.4.3 Inspection and testing of welded shear studs for composite steel and concrete structures<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Inspection and testing of welded shear studs for composite steel and concrete structures shall be carried out
according to EN ISO 14555.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This inspection includes checking the length of the studs after welding.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Non conforming studs shall be replaced. It is recommended that replacement studs be welded in an adjacent
new position.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The proper operation of welding equipment used on site should be rechecked after it has been moved and at
the commencement of each shift or other period of work by using tests on studs welded with the equipment in
accordance with EN ISO 14555.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.4.4 Production tests on welding<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If specified, for EXC3 and EXC4, production tests shall be carried out as follows:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
each welding procedure qualification used for welding steel grades higher than S460 shall be checked
with a production weld. Testing includes visual examination, penetrant testing or magnetic particle
inspection, ultrasonic testing or radiographic testing (for butt welds), hardness testing and macroscopic
examination. The tests and results shall be in accordance with the relevant standard for welding
procedure test;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
if the deep penetration of a welding process is used for fillet welds, the penetration of the welds shall be
checked. The results of the actual penetration shall be documented;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c)
for bridge deck orthotropic steel plates:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>1) stiffener to deckplate connections welded by fully mechanized welding process shall be checked with
a production test for each 120 m length of bridge, with a minimum of one production test for a bridge,
and inspected by macro-examination. Macro section tests shall be prepared at start or stop and at the
middle of the weld;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>2) stiffener to stiffener connections with splice plates shall be checked with a production test.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>92<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_97>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.5 Mechanical fastening<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.5.1 Inspection of non-preloaded bolted connections<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>All connections with non-preloaded mechanical fasteners shall be visually checked after they are bolted up
with the structure aligned locally.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Connections identified during snagging that do not have a full complement of bolts shall be checked for fit up
after the missing bolts have been installed.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Acceptance criteria and action to correct nonconformity shall be in accordance with 8.3 and 9.6.5.3.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If the nonconformity is due to differing ply thickness that exceeds the criteria specified in 8.1, the connection
shall be remade. Otherwise nonconformity may be corrected, if possible, by adjusting the local alignment of
the component.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Corrected connections shall be checked again on re-completion.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If an insulation system is required at junctions between stainless steel and other metals, the requirements for
checking the installation shall also be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.5.2 Inspection and testing of preloaded bolted connections<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.5.2.1
Inspection of friction surfaces<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If the connections incorporate friction surfaces the surfaces shall be visually checked immediately before
assembly. Acceptance criteria shall be in accordance with 8.4. Nonconformities shall be corrected in
accordance with 8.4.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If preloaded bolts are used for stainless steel connections, the requirements for inspection and testing shall be
specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.5.2.2
Inspection before tightening<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>All connections with preloaded mechanical fasteners shall be visually checked after they are initially bolted up
with the structure aligned locally and before the commencement of preloading. Acceptance criteria shall be in
accordance with 8.5.1.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If the nonconformity is due to differing ply thickness that exceeds the criteria specified in 8.1, the connection
shall be remade. Otherwise nonconformity may be corrected, if possible, by adjusting the local alignment of
component.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If chamfered washers are installed then they shall be visually checked to ensure that assembly is in
accordance with 8.2.4 and Annex J.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Corrected connections shall be checked on re-completion.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For EXC2, EXC3 and EXC4, the tightening procedure shall be checked. If tightening is carried out by the
torque method or the combined method, the torque wrench calibration certificates shall be checked to verify
the accuracy to 8.5.1.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.5.2.3
Inspection during and after tightening<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>In addition to the following general requirements for inspection, which apply to all tightening methods except
for the HRC method, particular requirements are given in 12.5.2.4 to 12.5.2.7.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For EXC2, EXC3 and EXC4, inspection during and after tightening shall be carried out as follows:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>93<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_98>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) inspection of installed fasteners and/or methods of installation shall be undertaken depending on the
tightening method used. The locations selected shall be on a random basis ensuring that the sampling
covers the following variables as appropriate - connection type; bolt group, fastener lot, type and size;
equipment used and the operatives;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) for the purposes of the inspection, a bolt group is defined as bolt assemblies of the same origin in similar
connections with the bolt assemblies of the same size and class. A large bolt group may be subdivided
into a number of subgroups for inspection purposes;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) the number of bolt assemblies inspected overall in a structure shall be as follows:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  EXC2: 5 % for the second step of the torque or the combined method and for the DTI method;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  EXC3 and EXC4:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>i. 5 % for the first step and 10% for the second step of the combined method;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>ii.  10 % for the second step of the torque method and for the DTI method;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) unless otherwise specified, the inspection shall be carried out using a sequential sampling plan according
to Annex M for a sufficient number of bolt assemblies until either the acceptance or the rejection
conditions (or all assemblies have been tested) for the relevant sequential type are met for the relevant
criteria. The sequential types shall be as follows:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  EXC2 and EXC3: sequential type A;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  EXC4: sequential type B;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) the pretightening step shall be checked by visual inspection of connections to ensure they are fully
packed;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f)
for final tightening inspection the same bolt assembly shall be used for checking both under-tightening
and, if specified, over-tightening;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>g) for the inspection of pretightening only the under-tightening criterion is to be checked;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>h) the criteria defining a nonconformity and requirements for corrective action are specified below for each
tightening method;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>i)
if the inspection leads to a rejection, all the bolting assemblies in the bolt subgroup shall be checked and
corrective actions shall be taken. If the result of inspection when using a sequential type A is negative, the
inspection may be enlarged to the sequential type B;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>j)
after completion a new inspection is required.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If fasteners are not applied in accordance with the defined method, the removal and re-installation of the
whole bolt group shall be witnessed.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.5.2.4
Torque method<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The inspection of a bolt assembly shall be carried out, using Table 25, by the application of a torque to the nut
(or to the bolt head if specified) using a calibrated torque wrench. The objective is to check that the torque
value necessary to initiate rotation is at least equal to 1,1 times the torque value  M r,i  (i.e  M r,2  or  M r, test ). Caution
shall be taken to keep the rotation to a strict minimum. The following conditions apply:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) the torque wrench used for the inspections shall be correctly calibrated and have an accuracy of
±  4 %;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>94<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_99>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) the inspection shall be carried out between 12 h and 72 h after final completion of tightening in the bolt
subgroup concerned;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 1 If the bolt assemblies to be inspected are from different assembly lots, with inspection torque values that
are different the locations of each lot should be established.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 2 If the contact surfaces are protection-coated, in particular if painted, the loss of preload can be such that
the satisfying of the criteria specified is not possible. Special inspection procedures, such as continuous
supervision of tightening, can be necessary in these circumstances.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) if the result is rejection, the accuracy of torque wrench used for tightening shall be checked.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Table 25 — Inspection of tightening by the torque method<<HEADING_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE   For assembly bolt lot definition, see EN 14399-1.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>A bolting assembly for which the nut turns by more than 15° by the application of the inspecting torque is
considered to be under-tightened (< 100 %) and shall be retightened up to 100 % of the required torque.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.5.2.5
Combined method<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For EXC3 and EXC4 the first step shall be controlled before marking using the same torque conditions as
used to reach the 75 % condition. A bolt which turns by more than 15° by the application of the inspecting
torque is considered defective and shall be retightened.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If the connections are not fully packed according to 8.3 and 8.5.1, the calibrations of the torque wrenches in
combination with the applied loads shall be controlled by supplementary tests to achieve the correct initial
pretightening load. If necessary, the first step has to be repeated with the corrected torque values.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If still unpacked, the thickness and out of plane of the assembled connections shall be inspected and
adjusted.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Before the second step starts, the markings of all the nuts relative to the bolt threads shall be visually
inspected. Any mark missing shall be corrected.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>After the second step, the marks shall be inspected with the following requirements:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
if the rotation angle is more than 15° below the specified value, this angle shall be corrected;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
if the rotation angle is more than 30° over the specified angle, or the bolt or the nut has failed, the bolt
assembly shall be replaced by new one.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.5.2.6
HRC method<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The inspection shall be carried out on 100 % of the bolting assemblies by visual inspection. Fully tightened
bolt assemblies are identified as those with the spline end sheared off. A bolt assembly for which the spline
end remains is considered to be under-tightened.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<PAGE_100>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If tightening of HRC bolting assemblies is completed using the torque method according to 8.5.3 or by the DTI
method to 8.5.6, they shall be inspected according to 12.5.2.4 or 12.5.2.7 as appropriate.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.5.2.7
Direct tension indicator method<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>After the pretightening step, connections shall be inspected to ensure that they are properly packed in
accordance with 8.3. The local alignment of non conforming connections shall be corrected before final
tightening commences.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>After final tightening, assemblies selected for inspection in accordance with 12.5.2.3 shall be checked to
establish that the final indicator settings are in accordance with the requirements in Annex J. The visual
inspection shall include a check to identify any indicators that exhibit full compression of the indicator. No
more than 10 % of the indicators in a connection bolt group shall exhibit full compression of the indicator.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If the fasteners are not installed in accordance with Annex J or if the final indicator setting is not within the
specified limits, the removal and reinstallation of the non conforming assembly shall be supervised, and the
whole bolt group shall then be inspected. If the direct tension indicator has not been tightened to the specified
limit, the assembly can be further tightened until this limit is achieved.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.5.3 Inspection, testing and repairs of hot rivets<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.5.3.1
Inspection<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The number of rivets inspected overall in a structure shall be at least 5 %, with a minimum of 5.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Heads of driven rivets shall be visually inspected and shall satisfy the acceptance criteria of 8.7.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Inspection of satisfactory contact shall de done by lightly ringing the rivet head with a hammer of
0,5 kg. The inspection is carried out using a sequential sampling plan according to Annex M to a sufficient
number of rivets until either the acceptance or the rejection conditions for the relevant sequential type are met
for the relevant criteria. The sequential types are as follows:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  EXC2 and EXC3: sequential type A;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  EXC4: sequential type B.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If the inspection leads to a rejection, all the rivets shall be checked and corrective actions shall be taken.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.5.3.2
Repairs<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If it is necessary to replace a defective rivet, it shall be done before the structure is loaded. Cutting out shall be
done by means of a chisel or by cutting.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>After removing a rivet, sides of the rivet hole shall be inspected carefully. In case of cracks, pits, or hole
distortion, the hole shall be reamed. If necessary, the replacement rivet shall be of a larger diameter than that
removed.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.5.4 Inspection of cold formed components and sheeting fastening<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.5.4.1
Self-tapping and self-drilling screws<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If using self-tapping screws, sample holes shall be measured periodically by spot checks on site to ensure that
they are in accordance with the fastener manufacturer's recommendations.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If using self-drilling and self-tapping screws on site, sampler screws shall be spot checked periodically to
ensure thread integrity after setting. This method is advisable for each different application. Fasteners which<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>96<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_101>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>exhibit a deformation of thread form exceeding the limits given by the fastener manufacturer shall be treated
as nonconforming and be replaced with new fasteners.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
The advice of the fastener manufacturer should be sought in respect of replacement fasteners. These can
need to be of a larger diameter to ensure a secure fixing in a pre-formed hole.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.5.4.2
Blind rivets<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Sample holes shall be measured periodically by spot checks on site to ensure that they are in accordance with
the product manufacturer’s recommendations.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Holes with burred edges that would adversely affect the drawing together of the connected parts shall be
treated as nonconforming until such time as they are rectified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Connections with blind rivets shall be inspected to ensure that the upset at the blind end of the rivet is not
formed between the overlapping sheets. Such connections shall be treated as nonconforming. The spoilt rivet
shall be removed and replaced.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If the spoilt rivet is removed with a drill of larger diameter than used to form the original hole the replacement
rivet shall be suitable for the hole size created.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.5.5 Special fasteners and fastening methods<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.5.5.1
General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Requirements for inspection of connections using special fasteners or special fastening methods in
accordance with 8.9 shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If tapped holes are used in cast materials, NDT around the tapped holes shall be carried out to ensure
material homogeneity.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.5.5.2
Cartridge fired and air driven pins<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Inspection shall be carried out to ensure that cartridge fired and air driven pins connections have not been
over or underdriven.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
If too powerful a power load is used there may be heavy indentation or excessive deformation of the washers
(overdriving). Insufficient penetration of the fastener is due to use of too light driving force (underdriving).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The manufacturer's identification mark on the pin shall still be recognizable after the fasteners have been
driven.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.5.5.3
Other mechanical fasteners<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Inspection of connections with other mechanical fasteners (such as, e.g. hook-bolts, special fasteners) shall
be applied according to national product standards/recommendations or manufacturers guidelines or specified
methods.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.6 Surface treatment and corrosion protection<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If the structure is to be protected against corrosion, inspection of the structure prior to corrosion protection
shall be carried out against the requirements of Clause 10.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>All surfaces, welds and edges shall be visually inspected.The acceptance criteria shall meet requirements of
EN ISO 8501.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Nonconforming components shall be retreated, retested and re-inspected afterwards.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The inspection of the corrosion protection shall be carried out according to Annex F.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>97<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_102>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.7 Erection<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.7.1 Inspection of trial erection<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Requirements for inspection of any trial erection to 9.6.4 shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.7.2 Inspection of the erected structure<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The condition of the erected structure shall be inspected for any indication that components have been
distorted or overstressed, and to ensure that any temporary attachments have either been removed
satisfactorily or are in accordance with the specified requirements.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.7.3 Survey of geometrical position of connection nodes<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.7.3.1
Survey methods and accuracy<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>A survey of the completed structure shall be made. This survey shall be related to the secondary net. For
EXC3 and EXC4 this survey shall be recorded; if there is a requirement to record dimensional checks at
acceptance of the structure, this shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Methods and instruments used shall be selected from those listed in ISO 7976-1 and ISO 7976-2. The
selection shall take into account the capability of the survey process in terms of accuracy relative to the
acceptance criteria. If appropriate, the survey shall be corrected for the effects of temperature and the
accuracy of the measurements relative to that in 9.4.1 shall be estimated according to the relevant parts of
ISO 17123.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
In most cases where surveys take place in ambient temperatures between 5 °C and 15 °C no correction is
necessary.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.7.3.2
System of measurement<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The system of permitted deviations is built up from position points at base level, an envelope for column
verticality and a series of intermediate and roof levels referred to as-built floor levels.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Position points mark the location of individual components for instance columns (see ISO 4463-1).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Each individual value shall be in accordance with the values from the figures and tables. The algebraic sum of
the discrete values shall not be greater than the permitted deviations for the total structure.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The system shall set out requirements for connection positions. Between these positions the manufacturing
tolerances define permitted deviations.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The system does not set out explicit requirements for secondary structural components such as side posts
and purlins.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Special attention will need to be given to establishing lines and levels when fitting to existing construction.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.7.3.3
Reference points and levels<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Erection tolerances shall generally be specified relative to the following reference points on each component:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) for components within 10° of the vertical: the centre of the component at each end;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) for components within 45° of the horizontal (including the tops of lattice trusses): the centre of the top
surface at each end;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) for internal components in built-up lattice girders and trusses: the centre of the component at each end;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>98<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_103>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) for other components: the erection drawings shall indicate the reference points which shall generally be
the top or outside surfaces of components mainly subject to bending and centre lines of components
mainly subject to direct compression or tension.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Alternative reference points may be substituted for ease of reference, provided that they have similar effect to
those specified above.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.7.3.4
Location and frequency<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Measurements will only be taken of the position of components adjacent to site interconnection nodes as set
out below, unless otherwise specified. The location and frequency of measurements shall be specified in the
inspection plan.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Critical dimensional checks of the as-built structure necessary in relation to special tolerances should be
identified and these should be incorporated into the inspection plan.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The positional accuracy of the erected steelwork should be measured under self weight of steelwork only
unless otherwise specified. The conditions under which the measurements shall take place shall then be
specified as well as the deviations and movements due to imposed loads, other than those due to self weight
of steelwork, if these can affect dimensional checks.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.7.3.5
Acceptance criteria<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The acceptance criteria are given in 11.2 and 11.3.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.7.3.6
Definition of nonconformity<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Assessment of whether a non conformity exists shall take into account the inevitable variability in methods of
measurement calculated in accordance with 12.7.3.1.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 1
ISO 3443-1 to -3 give guidance on tolerances for buildings and the implications of variabilities (including
manufacturing, setting-out and erection deviations) on the fit between components.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Accuracy of construction shall be interpreted in relation to the expected deflections, cambers, presets, elastic
movements and thermal expansion of components.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 2
EN 1993-1-4 gives values for the coefficient of thermal expansion for common stainless steels.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If significant movement of a structure is anticipated that could affect dimensional checking (e.g. for tension
structures) an envelope of permissible positions shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.7.3.7
Action on nonconformity<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Action on nonconformity shall be in accordance with 12.3. Corrections shall be carried out using methods that
are in accordance with this European Standard.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If a steel structure is handed over with uncorrected nonconformities awaiting action these shall be listed.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.7.4 Other acceptance tests<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If components of a structure are to be erected to a specific load rather than position, detailed requirements,
including tolerance range on the load shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>99<<HEADING_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>A.3 Requirements related to the execution classes<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This clause lists requirements specific to each of the execution classes referenced in this European Standard.
“Nr” in the table means: No specific requirement in the text.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Items identified in bold letters in Table A.3 relate to the general system of control of execution and are
amenable to a common choice of execution class across the whole of the works (or a phase of the works).
The other items generally demand the selection of the appropriate execution class on a component–by-
component or a connection detail-by-detail basis.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=2>>Annex B
(informative)
Guidance for the determination of execution classes<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>B.1 Introduction<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This annex provides guidance for the choice of execution classes with respect to those execution factors that
affect the overall reliability of the completed works and which is a prerequisite for the application of the various
clauses in this European Standard.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
The recommended procedure for determination and the use of execution class according to
EN 1090-2 takes into account the fact that the design will be carried out in accordance with EN 1993 for steel structures or
EN 1994 for the steel parts of composite structures to achieve consistency between the assumptions made in the
structural design and the requirements for execution of the work. The determination of execution class is done in the
design phase where specifics for design and execution of the structure are evaluated, and the information on execution
requirements are given in the execution specification. The guidelines in this annex may be wholly or partially superseded
by future guidelines added to EN 1993.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>B.2 Governing factors for choice of execution class<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>B.2.1 Consequence classes<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>EN 1990:2002 gives in its Annex B guidelines for the choice of consequence class for the purpose of reliability
differentiation. Consequence classes for structural components are divided in three levels denoted CCi (i = 1,
2 or 3).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Annex B in EN 1990:2002 is informative. Consequently the national annex to EN 1990 may give provisions for
the application of this annex.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>EN 1991-1-7 gives examples of categorisation of building type and occupancy according to consequence
classes that assist with the implementation of Annex B of EN 1990:2002.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>A structure, or a part of it, can contain components with different consequence classes.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>B.2.2 Hazards connected with execution and use of the structure<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>B.2.2.1
General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Such hazards may arise from the complexity of the work execution and from uncertainty in the exposure and
actions on the structure that can expose flaws in the structure during use.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Potential hazards are in particular connected with:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  service factors arising from the actions to which the structure and its parts are likely to be exposed to
during erection and use and the stress levels in the components in relation to their resistance;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  production factors arising from the complexity of the execution of the structure and its components, e.g.
application of particular techniques, procedures or controls.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>To account for this differentiation in hazards service categories and production categories are introduced.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>111<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_116>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>B.2.2.2
Hazards connected with the use of the structure<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The service category may be determined on the basis of Table B.1.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Table B.1 — Suggested criteria for service categories<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Categories
Criteria<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>SC1
•
Structures and components designed for quasi static actions only (Example:
Buildings)
•
Structures and components with their connections designed for seismic actions in
regions with low seismic activity and in DCL*
•
Structures and components designed for fatigue actions from cranes (class S 0 )**<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>•
Structures and components designed for fatigue actions according to EN 1993.
(Examples: Road and railway bridges, cranes (class S 1  to S 9 )**, structures
susceptible to vibrations induced by wind, crowd or rotating machinery)
•
Structures and components with their connections designed for seismic actions in
regions with medium or high seismic activity and in DCM* and DCH*
*  DCL, DCM, DCH: ductility classes according to EN 1998-1
** For classification of fatigue actions from cranes, see EN 1991-3 and EN 13001-1<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>SC2<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>A structure or part of a structure can contain components or structural details that belong to different service
categories.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>B.2.2.3
Hazards connected with execution of the structure<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The production category may be determined on the basis of Table B.2.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Table B.2 — Suggested criteria for production categories<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Categories
Criteria<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>PC1
•
Non welded components manufactured from any steel grade products
•
Welded components manufactured from steel grade products below S355<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>•
Welded components manufactured from steel grade products from S355 and
above
•
Components essential for structural integrity that are assembled by welding on
construction site
•
Components with hot forming manufacturing or receiving thermic treatment during
manufacturing
•
Components of CHS lattice girders requiring end profile cuts<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>PC2<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>A structure or part of a structure may contain components or structural details that belong to different
production categories.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>B.3 Determination of execution classes<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The recommended procedure for determination of execution class is in three steps:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) selection of a consequence class, expressed in terms of predictable consequences either human,
economical or environmental of a failure or collapse of a component (see EN 1990);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) selection of a service category and a production category (see Table B.1 and B.2);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) determination of the execution class from the results of the operations a) and b) according to
Table B.3.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>112<<HEADING_END>>

<<HEADING level=2>>Annex C
(informative)
Check-list for the content of a quality plan<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1 Introduction<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>In accordance with 4.2.2 this annex gives the list of recommended items to be included in a project-specific
quality plan for the execution of a steel structure.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2 Content<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.1 Management<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Definition of the particular steel structure and its location with relation to the project.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Project management organisation plan giving names key personnel, their function and responsibilities during
the project, the chain of command and lines of communication.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Arrangements for planning and coordination with other parties throughout the project and for monitoring of
performance and progress.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Identification of functions delegated to subcontractors and others not in-house.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Identification and proof of competence of qualified personnel to be employed on the project, including welding
coordination personnel, inspection personnel, welders and welding operators.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Arrangements for controlling variations, changes and concessions that take place during the project.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.2 Specification review<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Requirement to review the specified project requirements to identify the implications including the choices of
execution classes that would require additional or unusual measures beyond those assured by the company’s
quality management system.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Additional quality management procedures necessitated by the review of the specified project requirements.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.3 Documentation<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.3.1
General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Procedures to manage all received and issued execution documentation, including identification of the current
revision status and prevention of the use of invalid or obsolete documents in-house or by subcontractors.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.3.2
Documentation prior to execution<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Procedures for providing documentation prior to execution, including:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) certificates for constituent products including consumables;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) weld procedure specifications and qualification records;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>114<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_119>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) method statements including those for erection and preloading fasteners;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) design calculations for temporary works necessitated by the erection methods;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) arrangements for scope and timing of second or third party approval or acceptance of documentation prior
to execution.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.3.3
Execution records<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Procedures for providing execution records, including:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
constituent products traced to completed components;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
inspection and test reports and action taken to deal with nonconformities, concerning:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>1) Preparation of joint faces prior to welding,<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>2) Welding and completed weldments,<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>3) Geometrical tolerances of manufactured components,<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>4) Surface preparation and treatment,<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>5) Calibration of equipment including those used for control of preloading of fasteners;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c)
pre-erection survey results leading to acceptance that the site is suitable for erection to commence;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d)
delivery schedules for components delivered to site identified to location with the completed structure;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e)
dimensional surveys of the structure and action taken to deal with nonconformities;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f)
certificates for completion of erection and handover.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.3.4
Documentary records<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Arrangements for making documentary records available for inspection, and for retaining them for a minimum
period of five years, or longer if required by the project.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2.4 Inspection and testing procedures<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Identification of the mandatory tests and inspections required by the standard and those provided in the
constructor’s quality system that are necessary for the execution of the project, including:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) the scope of inspection;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) acceptance criteria;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) actions for dealing with nonconformities, corrections and concessions;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) release/rejection procedures.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Project-specific requirements for inspection and testing, including requirements that particular tests or
inspections are to be witnessed, or points where a nominated third party is to carry out an inspection.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Identification of hold points associated with second or third party witnessing, approval or acceptance of test or
inspection results.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>115<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_120>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>Misalignment:
Non-intended eccentricity of plates at a horizontal joint.
At a change of plate thickness, the intentional part of the
eccentricity is not included.
Class C

<<PARAGRAPH>>At a change of plate thickness:
t  = ( t 1  +  t 2 )/2
∆  =  e tot  -  e int
where
t 1  is the larger thickness;
t 2  is the smaller thickness .<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=2>>Annex E
(informative)
Welded joints in hollow sections<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>E.1 General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This annex gives guidance for execution of welded joints in hollow sections.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>E.2 Guidance for start and stop positions<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The following guidance may be used for in-line joints:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
stop and start positions of welds for in-line splice joints in chords should be chosen to avoid these
positions coming directly under the location of a subsequent weld between a brace and the chord;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
stop and start positions for welds between two in-line square or rectangular hollow sections should not
be located at or close to the corner positions.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The following guidance may be used for other joints:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c)
stop and start positions should not be located at or close to the toe position or lateral flank positions of a
joint between two circular hollow sections in accordance with Figure E.1;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d)
stop and start positions should not be located at or close to the corner positions of a joint between a
square or rectangular hollow section bracing and a hollow chord component;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e)
recommended welding sequence for welding brace to chord joints are given in Figure E.1;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f)
welding between hollow sections should be completed all round, even if this total length of weld is not
necessary for strength reasons.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<IMAGE_52>>
[Image 52 contains text: yO;]
<<HEADING level=3>>Figure E.1 — Start and stop positions and welding sequence<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>E.3 Preparation of joint faces<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>With reference to 7.5.1.2, examples of application of EN ISO 9692-1 to brace to chord joints between hollow
sections are given in Figures E.2 to E.5).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Recommendations for the weld preparation and fit-up for mitre butt joints are locally the same as for butt
welds between two components in-line, which requires the bevel angle to be increased on the inside of the
mitre and reduced on the outside as shown in Figure E.6.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>E.4 Assembly for welding<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>In accordance with 7.5.4 assembly of hollow section components to be welded shall be in accordance with the
following requirements:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
assembly using non-overlapping welding of the separate components is preferred (Case A in Figure E.7);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
assembly of overlapping components should be avoided; if necessary Case B in Figure E.7 is
acceptable;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c)
if components overlap (as Case B), the welding details shall specified which components are to be cut to
fit around other components;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d)
the hidden toe area (as Case B) has not to be welded otherwise specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>For joints not significantly subjected to dynamic loading, the following deviations may be permitted for the
alignment between the root edges or root faces of in-line butt joints between hollow section components:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
25 % of the thickness of the thinner constituent product for material  ≤ 12 mm thick;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
3 mm for material over 12 mm thick.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This alignment may be achieved using machining of ends to correct wall thickness variations and ovality or
out-of-squareness of hollow sections, provided that the remaining material thickness complies with the
minimum specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For in-line splice butt joints between hollow sections of different thickness, the thicknesses may be matched
using the following guidance in accordance with Figure E.8:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
if the difference in thickness does not exceed 1,5 mm, no special measures are necessary;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
if the difference in thickness does not exceed 3 mm, the backing material may be shaped to
accommodate the difference (local hot forming of the backing material may be used);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c)
if the difference exceeds 3 mm the wall of the thicker component should be tapered with a slope of 1 in 4
or less.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=2>>Annex F
(normative)
Corrosion protection<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>F.1
General<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>F.1.1 Field of application<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This Annex gives requirements and guidelines relating to the execution of corrosion protection undertaken off-
site and/or on-site on steel components with the exception of stainless steels. The field of application is
corrosion protection by means of surface preparation and application of paint systems or metallic coatings by
means of thermal spray or galvanizing. Cathodic protection is not included.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The requirements for corrosion protection shall be given in the execution specification in terms of a
performance specification or as performance requirements for the protective treatment to be used.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 1
EN ISO 12944-8 gives guidelines for developing specifications for corrosion protection using paints.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This annex does not cover the corrosion protection of cables and fittings.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 2
See Annex A of EN 1993-1-11:2006.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>F.1.2 Performance specification<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The performance specification shall specify:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
the expected life of the corrosion protection (see EN ISO 12944-1) and<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
the corrosivity category (see EN ISO 12944-2).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The performance specification may also state a preference for painting, thermal spraying or galvanizing.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>F.1.3 Prescriptive requirements<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If the expected life of a corrosion protection and corrosivity category are specified, prescriptive requirements
shall be developed to comply with them. Otherwise, the execution specification shall define the prescriptive
requirements giving details of the following items as are relevant:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
surface preparation for manufactured steel components to be painted (see F.2.1);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
surface preparation for manufactured steel components for thermal spraying (see EN 14616 and F.2.1);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c)
surface preparation for manufactured steel components to be galvanized (see F.2.2);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d)
processes for surface preparation of fasteners (see F.5);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e)
paint system in accordance with EN ISO 12944-5 and/or paint products that have had their performance
assessed according to EN ISO 12944-6. This may include requirements relevant to subsequent
decorative coatings and restrictions on choice of colour for coating products;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f)
work methods for initial application of paint products and repair (see EN ISO 12944-8 and F.6.1);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>172<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_177>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Repair on site of shop-applied coatings may require special consideration.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>g)
thermal spraying (see F.6.2);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>h)
galvanizing (see F.6.3);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>i)
particular requirements for inspection and checking (see F.7);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>j)
special requirements for bimetallic interfaces;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>k)
special requirements for sheetings.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>F.1.4 Work method<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Corrosion protection shall be undertaken in accordance with work methods that are based on a quality plan
and that comply with F.2 to F.6 as relevant. The quality plan shall be developed from the prescriptive
requirements in F.1.3.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Work methods shall identify whether work is to be undertaken pre- or post- manufacturing.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Corrosion protection products shall be used in accordance with the manufacturer's recommendations. Storage
and handling procedures for materials shall ensure that the materials to be used are within their shelf life and
pot life after opening or mixing.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>All painted, thermal sprayed or hot dip galvanized products shall be carefully handled, stored and transported
to avoid damage to their surfaces. Packing, wrapping and other materials used for handling and storage shall
generally be of non-metallic type.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Adequate well-ventilated space, protected against the influence of weather, moisture and other coating work
shall be provided to allow the paints to cure to an acceptable level and to avoid corrosion of metallic coatings.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>No handling, storage and transport shall be performed before the coating system is cured to an acceptable
level.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The curing time shall be not less than recommended by the product manufacturer.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Repair procedures shall be appropriate to the damage incurred using handling, storage and erection
procedures.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>F.2
Surface preparation of carbon steels<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>F.2.1 Surface preparation of carbon steels prior to painting and metal spraying<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Surfaces shall be prepared in accordance with EN ISO 12944-4, and EN ISO 8501.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Procedure tests shall be undertaken on blast cleaning processes to establish the surface cleanliness and
surface roughness achievable. These shall be repeated at intervals during production.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The results of procedure tests on blast cleaning processes shall be sufficient to establish that the process is
suitable for the subsequent coating process.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Measurement and assessment of surface roughness shall be undertaken according to EN ISO 8503-1 and
EN ISO 8503-2.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If coated materials are to receive further treatment, the surface preparation shall be appropriate to the
subsequent treatment.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>173<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_178>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 1
Abrasive cleaning and wire brushing are not appropriate to sound metallic or organically coated components.
However, if repairs to coatings are needed, it may be necessary to remove debris or corrosion deposits locally to reveal
the basic steel substrate before carrying out the repair.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If overpainting of zinc coated steel is carried out, the cleaning of the surface requires particular attention.
Surfaces shall be cleaned (removal of dust and grease) and possibly treated with a suitable etch primer or
sweepblasting according to EN ISO 12944-4 to surface roughness “fine” in accordance with EN ISO 8503-2.
The pre-treatment shall be checked before subsequent overcoating.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 2
Pre-coated galvanized steel strip is often supplied with a chromate passivation.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>F.2.2 Surface preparation of carbon steels prior to galvanizing<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Surfaces shall be prepared in accordance with EN ISO 8501 and EN ISO 1461 unless otherwise specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>With pickling used prior to galvanizing, high strength steels may become susceptible to hydrogen-inducing
cracking (see Annex C of EN ISO 1461:1999).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>F.3
Welds and surfaces for welding<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If a component is subsequently to be welded, the surfaces of the component within 150 mm of the weld shall
not be coated with materials that will impair the quality of the weld (see also 7.5.1.1).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Welds and adjacent parent metal shall not be painted before de-slagging, cleaning, checking and acceptance
of the weld (see also 10.2 - Table 22).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>F.4
Surfaces in preloaded connections<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For slip resistant connections, the execution specification shall specify requirements for friction surfaces and
class of treatment or tests required (see 8.4 and 12.5.2.1).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For preloaded connections that are not required to be slip resistant, the extent of surfaces that are affected by
the preloaded bolts shall be specified. If the contact surfaces are to be painted before assembly the dry
coating thickness shall be between 100 µm and 75 µm. After assembly and preload, the connections shall be
cleaned and finally painted with the relevant system.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>F.5
Preparation of fasteners<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The specification for the preparation of fasteners shall be consistent with the following:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
the corrosion protection classification specified for the work or part of work;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
the material and type of fastener;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c)
the adjacent materials in contact with the fastener when in position and coatings on those materials;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d)
the method of tightening the fastener;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e)
the prospective need to repair the fastener treatment after tightening.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If preparation to fasteners is necessary after installation, it shall not be undertaken until the necessary
inspection of the fastener has been completed.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>174<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_179>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The embedded part of foundation bolts shall be protected for at least the first 50 mm below the finished
surface of the concrete. The remaining surfaces of the steel are to be left untreated unless otherwise specified
(see EN ISO 12944-3).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>F.6
Coating methods<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>F.6.1
Painting<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The surface condition of the component shall be checked immediately prior to painting to ensure that it
complies with the required specifications, EN ISO 12944-4, EN ISO 8501 and EN ISO 8503-2 and the
manufacturer's recommendations for the product about to be applied.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Painting shall be undertaken in accordance with EN ISO 12944-7.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If two or more coats are to be applied, a different colour shade shall be used for each coat.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Structures with an expected life of the corrosion protection above 5 years with a C3 (and above) corrosivity
category should have additional edge protection, by a stripe coat, extending across approximately 25 mm on
both side of the edge and applied to a nominal thickness appropriate to the coating system.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Work shall not proceed if:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  the ambient temperature is below that recommended in the manufacturer's recommendations for the
product to be applied;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  the surfaces to be coated are wet;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  the temperature of the surfaces to be coated is less than 3 °C above the dew point unless otherwise
specified in the product datasheet.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Painted surfaces shall be protected against the accumulation of water for a period after application as required
by the product data sheet.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The packing of painted components into bundles shall not commence until the paint manufacturer's declared
hardening time has expired. Adequate well ventilated space, protected against the influence of weather, shall
be provided to allow the coating to harden sufficiently. Appropriate measures shall be taken to prevent
damage to the coating during packing and handling.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE  Cold formed components are often produced as nesting profiles. Tightly packing components into
nested bundles before the paint treatment is sufficiently hardened may result in damage.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>F.6.2 Metal spraying<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Thermal metal spraying shall be of zinc, aluminium or zinc/aluminium 85/15 alloy and be undertaken in
accordance with EN ISO 2063.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Thermal metal sprayed surfaces shall be treated with a suitable sealer before overcoating with paint in
accordance with F.6.1. This sealer shall be compatible with the overcoating paint and shall be applied
immediately after metal spraying cooling so as to avoid oxidation or moisture trapping.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>F.6.3 Galvanizing<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Galvanizing shall be undertaken in accordance with EN ISO 1461.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Galvanized surfaces of cold-formed components shall be provided by using precoated steel strip or by hot dip
galvanizing after manufacturing.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>175<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_180>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 1
Coating masses, finishes and surface qualities are specified in EN 10326 and EN 10327.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If hot dip galvanizing after manufacturing is specified, it shall be undertaken in accordance with
EN ISO 1461 and requirements for procedure qualification of the dipping process shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 2
Light gauge cold-formed components often lack inherent stiffness. Long components composed of thin
material can be susceptible to twisting due to stress relieving at the elevated temperature of the zinc bath.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Requirements for the inspection, checking or qualification of the preparation to be carried out before
subsequent overcoating shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>F.7
Inspection and checking<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>F.7.1 General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Inspection and checking shall be undertaken in accordance with the quality plan and F.7.2 to F.7.4. The
execution specification shall specify any requirements for additional inspection and testing.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Inspection and checking, including routine checking to F.7.2, shall be recorded.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>F.7.2 Routine checking<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Routine checking of corrosion protection shall comprise:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) checks that prepared steel surfaces which are to receive corrosion protection treatment have the specified
degree of cleanliness, assessment in accordance with EN ISO 8501 and the specified surface roughness,
assessment in accordance with EN ISO 8503-2;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) thickness measurement of:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>1) each layer of the paint coating in accordance with ISO 19840 and EN ISO 2808;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>2) thermal spraying in accordance with EN ISO 2063;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>3) galvanizing in accordance with EN ISO 1461.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>4) Visual inspection that paint treatment complies with the provisions of EN ISO 12944-7.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>F.7.3 Reference areas<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>In accordance with EN ISO 12944-7, the execution specification shall define any reference areas to be used
to establish the minimum acceptable standard for the work. Unless otherwise specified, reference areas shall
be specified for corrosion protection systems in Corrosivity Categories C3 to C5 and Im1 to Im3.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>F.7.4 Galvanized components<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Unless otherwise specified, due to the risk of liquid metal assisted cracking (LMAC), galvanized components
shall be subjected to post-galvanizing inspection.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Information on LMAC is given in [51].<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The component specification shall specify the following:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
components for which post-galvanizing inspection is not required;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>176<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_181>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
components or specific locations that shall be subjected to additional NDT, the scope and method of
which shall be specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The results of post-galvanizing inspection shall be recorded.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If evidence of cracking is identified, then the component and all similarly shaped components fabricated with
similar materials and weld details shall be identified and quarantined as nonconforming products. A
photographic record of the cracking shall be made and a specific procedure shall then be used to establish the
scope and origin of the problem.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>177<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_182>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=2>>Annex G
(normative)
Test to determine slip factor<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>G.1 General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The purpose of this test is to determine the slip factor for a particular surface treatment, often involving a
surface coating.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The test procedure is intended to ensure that account is taken of the possibility of creep deformation of the
connection.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The validity of the test results for coated surfaces is limited to cases where all significant variables are similar
to those of the test specimens.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>G.2 Significant variables<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The following variables shall be taken as significant on the test results:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a)
the composition of the coating;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b)
the surface treatment and treatment of primary layers in case of multi-layer systems, see G.3;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c)
the maximum thickness of the coating, see G.3;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d)
the curing procedure;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e)
the minimum time interval between application of the coating and application of load to the connection;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>f)
the property class of the bolt, see G.6.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>G.3 Test specimens<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The test specimens shall conform to the dimensional details shown in Figure G.1.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The steel material shall conform to EN 10025-2 to -6.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>To ensure that the two inner plates have the same thickness, they shall be produced by cutting them
consecutively from the same piece of material and assembled in their original relative positions.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The plates shall have accurately cut edges that do not interfere with contact between the plate surfaces. They
shall be sufficiently flat to permit the prepared surfaces to be in contact when the bolts have been preloaded in
accordance with 8.1 and 8.5.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>178<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_183>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Dimensions in millimetres<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<IMAGE_60>>
[Image 60 contains text: fel ee
in aE!]
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) M20 bolts in 22 mm dia holes
b) M16 bolts in 18 mm dia holes<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Figure G.1 — Standard test specimens for slip factor test<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The specified surface treatment and coating shall be applied to the contact surfaces of the test specimens in a
manner consistent with the intended structural application. The mean coating thickness on the contact surface
of the test specimens shall be at least 25 % thicker than the nominal thickness specified for use in the
structure.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The curing procedure shall be documented, either by reference to published recommendations or by
description of the actual procedure.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The specimens shall be assembled such that the bolts are bearing in the opposite direction to the applied
tension.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The time interval (in hours) between coating and testing shall be recorded.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The bolts shall be tightened to within ± 5 % of the specified preload,  F p,C , for the size and property class of the
bolt used.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The preload in the bolts shall be directly measured with equipment that is accurate to ± 5 %.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
If it is required to estimate bolt preload losses over time, the test specimens may be left for a specified period
at the end of which the preloads may be again measured.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The bolt preloads in each test specimen shall be measured just prior to testing and, if necessary, the bolts
shall be retightened to the required ± 5 % accuracy.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>G.4  Slip test procedure and evaluation of results<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Initially, five test specimens shall be tested. Four tests shall be loaded at normal speed (duration of test
approximately 10 min to 15 min). The fifth test specimen shall be used for the creep test.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The specimens shall be tested in a tension loading machine. The load-slip relationship shall be recorded.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>179<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_184>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The slip shall be taken as the relative displacement between adjacent points on an inner plate and a cover
plate, in the direction of the applied load. It shall be measured for each end of the specimen separately. For
each end, the slip shall be taken as the mean of the displacements on both sides of the specimen.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The individual slip load for a connection,  F Si , is defined as the load at which a slip of 0,15 mm occurs.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The fifth test specimen shall be loaded with a specific load of 90 % of the mean slip load  F Sm  from the first four
specimens (i.e. the mean of eight values).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If for the fifth specimen the delayed slip, i.e. difference between the recorded slip at five minutes and at three
hours after the application of the full load does not exceed 0,002 mm the slip loads for the fifth test specimen
shall be determined as for the first four. If the delayed slip exceeds 0,002 mm extended creep tests shall be
carried out in accordance with G.5.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If the standard deviation  s Fs  of the ten values (obtained from the five test specimens) for the slip load exceeds
8 % of the mean value, additional specimens shall be tested. The total number of test specimens (including
the first five) shall be determined from:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>n  > ( s /3,5) 2<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>where<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>n   is the number of test specimens;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>s   is the standard deviation  s Fs  for the slip load from the first five specimens (ten values) expressed as a
percentage of the mean slip load value.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>G.5  Extended creep test procedure and evaluation<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If it is necessary to carry out extended creep tests, following G.4 at least three test specimens (six
connections) shall be tested.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>A specific load shall be applied to the test specimen whose value shall be determined so as to account both
for the result of the creep test carried out in G.4 and for the results of all preceding extended creep tests.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
A load corresponding to the slip factor proposed for use in the structural application may be adopted. If the
surface treatment is to belong to a specified class, a load corresponding to the slip factor for that class may be taken in
accordance with Table 18.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>A “displacement - log time” curve shall be plotted (see Figure G.2) to demonstrate that the load determined
using the proposed slip factor will not cause displacements greater than 0,3 mm during the design life of the
structure, taken as 50 years unless otherwise specified. The “displacement - log time curve” may be
extrapolated linearly as soon as the tangent can be determined with sufficient accuracy.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>The characteristic value of the slip factor  µ  shall be taken as the 5 % fractile value with a confidence level of

value.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=2>>Annex H
(normative)
Test to determine torque values for preloaded bolts under site conditions<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>H.1 Scope<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This Annex specifies a tightening test intended to represent site conditions to calibrate high-strength bolting
assemblies for preloaded bolted connections.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The purpose of the test is to determine the necessary parameters to ensure that the minimum required
preload is reliably obtained by the tightening methods specified in this European standard.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>H.2
Symbols and units<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>A s
nominal stress area of the bolt, (mm 2 ) (see EN ISO 898-1)
e M
allowable ratio  (e M  =  M max  – M min )/M m
F b
bolt force during the test, (kN)
F p,C
required preload of 0,7  f ub   A s , (kN)
f ub
nominal bolt strength ( R m ), (MPa)
M i
individual value of the torque related to  F p,C , (N m)
M m
mean value of  M i   values, (N m)
M max
maximum value of  M i   values, (N m)
M min
minimum value of  M i   values, (N m)
s M
estimated standard deviation of the  M i   values
V M
coefficient of variation of the  M i   values
θ pi
individual value of the angle  θ  at which the bolt force has first reached the value of  F p,C , (°)
θ 1i
individual value of the angle  θ  at which the bolt force has reached its maximum value  F bi , max , (°)
θ 2i
individual value of the angle  θ  at which the test is stopped, (°)
∆ θ 1i
the individual angle difference ( θ 1i   -  θ pi ), (°)
∆ θ 2i
the individual angle difference ( θ 2i  -  θ pi ), (°)
∆ θ 2 min   the minimum required value of the angle difference  ∆ θ 2i  as specified in the relevant product standard (°)<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>H.3 Principle of the test<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The principle of the test is to tighten assemblies and to measure, during tightening, the following parameters:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>•
the bolt force;
•
the torque;
•
the relative rotation between the nut and the bolt, if required.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>H.4 Test apparatus<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The bolt force measuring device may be in accordance with EN 14399-2, or a mechanical or hydraulic device
such as a load cell, provided the accuracy of the bolt force measuring device meets the requirements given in
Table H.1 or H.2 as relevant. The bolt force measuring device shall be calibrated at least once per year (or
more frequently if recommended by the equipment manufacturer) by a recognized testing authority.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Torque wrenches to be used for the test shall be one of those to be used on site. They shall offer suitable
operating range. Hand or power wrenches may be used, with exception of impact wrenches. The accuracy<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>183<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_188>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>requirements for the wrenches are given in Table H.1 or H.2 as relevant. The torque wrench shall be
calibrated at least once per year (or more frequently if recommended by the manufacturer).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>H.5 Test assemblies<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Separate tests shall be carried out on representative samples from each lot of fastener assemblies concerned.
Test assemblies shall be chosen so that all relevant aspects of their conditions are similar.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
The site conditions of fasteners, in particular the performance of the lubrication, can vary if they are left
exposed to extreme environmental conditions on site or if they are stored for a long period of time.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Representative assemblies shall consist of a number of bolts, nuts and washers of each inspection lot. The
assemblies used for tests shall not be re-used for supplementary tests or in the structure.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>H.6 Test set up<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The test set-up (see Figure H.1) may include shims needed to suit the measuring device.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The test assemblies and shims shall be positioned such that:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  the composition of the assembly is similar to the utilisation in practice;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  a chamfered washer or a chamfered shim is placed under the bolt head;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  a washer is placed under the nut when the nut will be turned during tightening;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  the clamp length including the shims and washer(s) is the minimum allowed in the relevant product
standard.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>184<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_189>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>Key<<HEADING_END>>
