<<HEADING level=3>>Figure H.1  —  Typical assembly of the tension measuring device<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>H.7 Test procedure<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For site tests the method used for tightening during the test shall be the same as that used on the site. For site
tests the basis of calibration is to record the torque values M i  needed to achieve the target preload tension in
the bolt.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Tests may be carried out either in a laboratory or elsewhere under suitable conditions. The method used for
tightening shall be the same as that to be used on the site.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
In certain cases it may be more convenient to have the product manufacturer check whether fastener
assemblies still meet the declared as-delivered properties.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>185<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_190>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Sufficient measurements shall be taken of the torque, the corresponding bolt tension and, if required, the
corresponding rotation of the turned part so as to permit the evaluation of the test results in accordance with
H.8.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Neither the fixed part nor the washer under the turned part shall rotate during the test.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The basis of calibration is to record the torque values  M i  needed to achieve the bolt force  F b  =  F p,C  =  0,7  f ub   A s .<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The test shall be terminated when any one of the following conditions is satisfied:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  the bolt force exceeds 1,1  F p,C ;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  the angle of nut rotation exceeds ( θ pi   +  ∆ θ 1 ) and/or ( θ pi   +  ∆ θ 2 min ), if required;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  bolt failure by fracture occurs.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>H.8 Evaluation of test results<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The criteria for acceptance of the torque values for the combined method and for the torque method are given
in Tables H.1 and H.2 respectiveley.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>H.9 Test report<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The following minimum information shall be included in the test report:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  date of testing;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  identification number of the assembly lot or the extended assembly lot;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  number of assemblies tested;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  designation of the fasteners;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  marking of bolts, nuts and washers;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  coating or surface finish and lubrication condition; if relevant, description of alterations to the surfaces due
to site exposure;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  test clamp length;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>  details of the test set-up and devices used to measure tension and torque;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>     remarks concerning the execution of tests (including special testing conditions and procedures such as
turning the head of the bolt);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>     tests results according to this annex;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>     specifications for the preloading of the fasteners related to the inspection lot tested.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The test report shall be signed and dated.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=2>>Annex J
(normative)
Use of compressible washer-type direct tension indicators<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>J.1 General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This annex gives requirements for the fitting and checking of compressible washer-type direct tension
indicators.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>J.2 Fitting<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Indicators are generally fitted under the bolt head and the bolt is generally tightened by rotation of the nut, as
shown in Figure J.1 a). Limited access to the bolt head for the purposes of inspecting the indicator gap may
require the indicator to be fitted under the nut. If used in this manner the appropriate nut face washer is fitted
between the indicator protrusions and the nut (see Figure H 1 b)).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=2>>Annex K
( informative)
Hexagon injection bolts<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>K.1 General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This annex provides information on the supply and use of hexagon injection bolts.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Injection bolts may be used as non-preloaded or preloaded bolts, as specified. Filling of the clearance
between the bolt and the inside surface of the hole is carried out through a small hole in the head of the bolt
as shown in Figure K.1. After injection and complete curing of the resin, the connection is slip resistant.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<IMAGE_65>>
[Image 65 contains text: ; 2
i.
tas]
<<PARAGRAPH>>4<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Key
1   injection hole
2   chamfered washer
3   resin
4   air escape groove in the washer<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Figure K.1 — Injection bolt in a double lap joint<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Injection bolts should be made of materials in accordance with Clause 5 and used in accordance with
Clause 8 supplemented by the recommendations in this annex.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Detailed information is given in [50].<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>K.2 Hole sizes<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The nominal clearance for bolts in the hole should be 3 mm. For bolts smaller than M27 the clearance may be
reduced to the clearance of 2 mm, as specified in 6.6 for normal round holes.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>K.3 Bolts<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The head of the bolt should be provided with a hole having a position and dimensions as specified in Figure
K.2.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>193<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_198>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If other types of nozzle than plastic nozzles are used, the edge may need to be chamfered in order to
guarantee sufficient sealing.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Dimensions in millimetres<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>Key<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>1   nozzle of injection device<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Figure K.2 — Hole in the head of the bolt<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>K.4 Washers<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Under the bolt head a special washer should be used. The inner diameter of this washer should be at least 0,5
mm larger than the actual diameter of the bolt. One side should be machined according to Figure K.3 a) or K.3
b).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) Drilled
b) Chamfered<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Figure K.3 — Preparation of the washer for use under the bolt head<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The washer under the bolt head should be positioned with the rebate towards the bolt head.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Under the nut a special washer provided with a groove according to Figure K.4 should be used. The edges of
the groove should be smooth and rounded.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The washer under the nut should be positioned with the groove towards the nut.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>194<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_199>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>Key<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>1   groove<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Figure K.4 — Preparation of the washer for use under the nut<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>K.5 Nuts<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The nuts may be assumed to be sufficiently secured by the resin.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>K.6 Resin<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>A two component resin should be used.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>After the mixing of the two components, the mass should have such a viscosity, at the ambient temperature
during installation, that the narrow spaces in the bolted connection will be filled easily. However, the flowing of
the mass should stop after the injection pressure has been removed.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The potlife of the resin should be at least 15 min at the ambient temperature.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If there are no data available, procedure tests should be carried out to determine the appropriate temperature
and curing time.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The design bearing strength of the resin should be determined similar to the procedure for the determination
of the slip factor as specified in Annex G.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>K.7 Tightening<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Tightening of the bolts in accordance with Clause 8 should be carried out before starting the injection
procedure.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>K.8 Installation<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The installation should be carried out in accordance with the recommendations given by the product
manufacturer.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The temperature of the resin should be between 15 °C and 25 °C. In very cold weather the resin and if
necessary the steel components should be preheated. If the temperature is too high, modelling clay may be
used to close the hole in the head and the groove in the washer immediately after injection.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The connection should be free from water at the time of injection.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>195<<HEADING_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_200>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BS EN 1090-2:2008<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Licensed Copy: Dr. Roger Pope, British Constructional Steelwork, 05/01/2009 21:37, Uncontrolled Copy, (c) BSI<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>EN 1090-2:2008 (E)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 1
To get rid of the water one day of dry weather is generally necessary before starting the injection procedure.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The curing time should be such that the resin is cured before the structure is loaded.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Heating after injection is permitted in order to reduce the curing time, if necessary.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE 2
In some cases e.g. the repair of railway bridges, this time can be rather short. To reduce the curing time (to
about 5 h) the connection may be heated to a maximum of 50 °C after the potlife has passed.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=2>>Annex M
(normative)
Sequential method for fasteners inspection<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>M.1
General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The sequential method for fasteners inspection shall be carried out according to the principles in
ISO 2859-5, the purpose of which being to give rules based on progressive determination of inspection
results.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>ISO 2859-5 gives two methods for establishing sequential sampling plans: numerical method and graphic
method. The graphic method is applied for fasteners inspection.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>In the graphic method (see Figure M.1) the horizontal axis is the number of fasteners inspected and the
vertical axis the number of defective fasteners.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The lines on the graph define three zones: the acceptance zone, the rejection zone and the indecision zone.
As long as the inspection result is in the indecision zone the inspection is continued until the cumulative plot
emerges into either the acceptance zone or the rejection zone. Acceptance means that no further sample
inspection is required. Two examples are given below.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<IMAGE_68>>
[Image 68 contains text: a ea
CC Saaeere yt TT a
Celery
A B
Beer a
Pt Dele | TT
CET te :]
<<HEADING level=3>>Key
1   number of fasteners inspected
2   number of defective fasteners
3   rejection zone
4   indecision zone
5   acceptance zone<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Figure M.1 — Example of sequential inspection diagram<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>EXAMPLES<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Dotted line
The 4th and 8th fasteners were found defective. Inspection was continued until crossing the vertical
curtailment line. The result is ”acceptance”.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

zone. The result is ”rejection”.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=1>>BSI - British Standards Institution<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BSI is the independent national body responsible for preparing British
Standards. It presents the UK view on standards in Europe and at the
international level. It is incorporated by Royal Charter.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Revisions<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>British Standards are updated by amendment or revision. Users of British
Standards should make sure that they possess the latest amendments or
editions.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>It is the constant aim of BSI to improve the quality of our products and services.
We would be grateful if anyone finding an inaccuracy or ambiguity while using
this British Standard would inform the Secretary of the technical committee
responsible, the identity of which can be found on the inside front cover. Tel:
+44 (0)20 8996 9000. Fax: +44 (0)20 8996 7400.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>BSI offers members an individual updating service called PLUS which ensures
that subscribers automatically receive the latest editions of standards.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Buying standards<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Orders for all BSI, international and foreign standards publications should be
addressed to Customer Services. Tel: +44 (0)20 8996 9001. Fax: +44 (0)20 8996
7001 Email: orders@bsigroup.com You may also buy directly using a debit/credit
card from the BSI Shop on the Website http://www.bsigroup.com/shop<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>In response to orders for international standards, it is BSI policy to supply the
BSI implementation of those that have been published as British Standards,
unless otherwise requested.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
